Why is Java a platform independent language?\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cp\u003EJava language was developed so that it does not depend on any hardware or software because the \u003Cstrong\u003Ecompiler\u003C/strong\u003E compiles the code and then converts it to platform-independent byte code which can be run on multiple systems.\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cul\u003E\u003Cli\u003EThe only condition to run that byte code is for the machine to have a runtime environment (JRE) installed in it.\u003C/li\u003E\u003C/ul\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https://www.scaler.com/topics/why-java-is-platform-independent/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"\"\u003ELearn More\u003C/a\u003E\u003C/p\u003E\n \u003C/div\u003E\n \u003C/div\u003E\n\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"java-not-purely-object-oriented-language\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E2. Why is Java not a pure object oriented language?\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cp\u003EJava supports primitive data types - byte, boolean, char, short, int, float, long, and double and hence it is not a pure \u003Ca href=\"https://www.interviewbit.com/oops-interview-questions/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"\"\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003Eobject oriented language\u003C/strong\u003E\u003C/a\u003E.\u003C/p\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"heap-vs-stack-memory-how-java-utilizes-this\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E3. Difference between Heap and Stack Memory in java. And how java utilizes this.\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cp\u003EStack memory is the portion of memory that was assigned to every individual program. And it was fixed. On the other hand, Heap memory is the portion that was not allocated to the java program but it will be available for use by the java program when it is required, mostly during the runtime of the program.\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EJava Utilizes this memory as - \u003C/strong\u003E\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cul\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EWhen we write a java program then all the variables, methods, etc are stored in the stack memory.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EAnd when we create any object in the java program then that object was created in the heap memory. And it was referenced from the stack memory.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003C/ul\u003E\u003Cp\u003EExample- \u003Cstrong\u003EConsider the below java program\u003C/strong\u003E:\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cpre\u003E\u003Ccode class=\"language-java hljs\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-class\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eclass\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-title\"\u003EMain\u003C/span\u003E \u003C/span\u003E{\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-function\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Epublic\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Evoid\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-title\"\u003EprintArray\u003C/span\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-params\"\u003E(\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eint\u003C/span\u003E[] array)\u003C/span\u003E\u003C/span\u003E{\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Efor\u003C/span\u003E(\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eint\u003C/span\u003E i : array)\n System.out.println(i);\n }\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-function\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Epublic\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Estatic\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Evoid\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-title\"\u003Emain\u003C/span\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-params\"\u003E(String args[])\u003C/span\u003E \u003C/span\u003E{\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eint\u003C/span\u003E[] array = \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Enew\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eint\u003C/span\u003E[\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-number\"\u003E10\u003C/span\u003E];\n printArray(array);\n }\n}\u003C/code\u003E\u003C/pre\u003E\u003Cp\u003EFor this java program. The stack and heap memory occupied by java is -\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cfigure class=\"image image_resized\" style=\"width:75%;\"\u003E\u003Cimg data-src=\"https://d3n0h9tb65y8q.cloudfront.net/public_assets/assets/000/003/020/original/stack_and_heap_memory.png?1648813762\" class=\"lazy-elem\"\u003E\u003C/figure\u003E\u003Cp\u003EMain and PrintArray is the method that will be available in the stack area and as well as the variables declared that will also be in the stack area. \u003C/p\u003E\u003Cp\u003EAnd the Object (Integer Array of size 10) we have created, will be available in the Heap area because that space will be allocated to the program during runtime. \u003C/p\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"can-java-be-said-to-be-the-complete-object-oriented-programming-language\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E4. Can java be said to be the complete object-oriented programming language?\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cp\u003EIt is not wrong if we claim that Java is the complete object-oriented programming language because everything in Java is under the classes and we can access them by creating the objects.\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cp\u003EBut we can even say that Java is not a completely object-oriented programming language because it has the support of primitive data types like int, float, char, boolean, double, etc.\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cp\u003ENow for the question: \u003Cstrong\u003EIs Java a completely object-oriented programming language?\u003C/strong\u003E We can say that - Java is not a pure object-oriented programming language, because it has direct access to primitive data types. And these primitive data types don't directly belong to the Integer classes.\u003C/p\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"how-is-java-different-from-cpp\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E5. How is Java different from C++?\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cul\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EC++ is only a compiled language, whereas Java is compiled as well as an interpreted language.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EJava programs are machine-independent whereas a c++ program can run only in the machine in which it is compiled. \u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EC++ allows users to use pointers in the program. Whereas java doesnt allow it. Java internally uses pointers. \u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EC++ supports the concept of Multiple inheritances whereas Java doesn't support this. And it is due to avoiding the complexity of name ambiguity that causes the diamond problem.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003C/ul\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n \u003Cdiv class=\"ib-articles-scaler-courses\"\u003E\n\n \u003Cdiv class=\"tracks-page-section-topics-courses m-v-20\"\u003E\n \u003Ch2 class=\"tracks-page-section-topics-courses__heading\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg\n class=\"tracks-page-section-topics-courses__heading-icon\"\n src=\"https://assets.interviewbit.com/assets/ibpp/interview_guides/monitor-play-834f8d9483abe09ad7c1d6449d2f7d188030cb9cef5137e09a374ce4a61cbbfd.svg.gz\"\n \u003E\n Learn via our Video Courses\n \u003C/h2\u003E\n \u003Cdiv class=\"tracks-page-section-topics-courses__carousel-container\"\u003E\n \u003Cdiv class=\"tracks-page-section-topics-courses__carousel-nav\"\u003E\n \u003Cbutton\n data-class=\"scaler-topics-course-carousel-left\"\n class=\"tracks-page-section-topics-courses__carousel-btn\"\n \u003E\n \u003Ci class=\"icon-chevron-left\"\u003E\u003C/i\u003E\n \u003C/button\u003E\n \u003Cbutton\n data-class=\"scaler-topics-course-carousel-right\"\n class=\"tracks-page-section-topics-courses__carousel-btn\"\n \u003E\n \u003Ci class=\"icon-chevron-right\"\u003E\u003C/i\u003E\n \u003C/button\u003E\n \u003C/div\u003E\n \u003Cdiv \n class=\"tracks-page-section-topics-courses__container\"\n data-class=\"scaler-topics-course-carousel\"\n \u003E\u003C/div\u003E\n \u003C/div\u003E\n \u003C/div\u003E\n\u003C/div\u003E\n\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"why-dont-we-use-pointers-in-java\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E6. Pointers are used in C/ C++. Why does Java not make use of pointers?\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cp\u003EPointers are quite complicated and unsafe to use by beginner programmers. Java focuses on code simplicity, and the usage of pointers can make it challenging. Pointer utilization can also cause potential errors. Moreover, security is also compromised if pointers are used because the users can directly access memory with the help of pointers.\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThus, a certain level of abstraction is furnished by not including pointers in Java. Moreover, the usage of pointers can make the procedure of garbage collection quite slow and erroneous. Java makes use of references as these cannot be manipulated, unlike pointers.\u003C/p\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"instance-variables-and-local-variables-in-java\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E7. What do you understand by an instance variable and a local variable?\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EInstance variables\u003C/strong\u003E are those variables that are accessible by all the methods in the class. They are declared outside the methods and inside the class. These variables describe the properties of an object and remain bound to it at any cost.\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cp\u003EAll the objects of the class will have their copy of the variables for utilization. If any modification is done on these variables, then only that instance will be impacted by it, and all other class instances continue to remain unaffected.\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EExample:\u003C/strong\u003E\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cpre\u003E\u003Ccode class=\"language-java hljs\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-class\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eclass\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-title\"\u003EAthlete\u003C/span\u003E \u003C/span\u003E{\n\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Epublic\u003C/span\u003E String athleteName;\n\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Epublic\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Edouble\u003C/span\u003E athleteSpeed;\n\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Epublic\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eint\u003C/span\u003E athleteAge;\n}\u003C/code\u003E\u003C/pre\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003ELocal variables\u003C/strong\u003E are those variables present within a block, function, or constructor and can be accessed only inside them. The utilization of the variable is restricted to the block scope. Whenever a local variable is declared inside a method, the other class methods dont have any knowledge about the local variable.\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EExample:\u003C/strong\u003E\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cpre\u003E\u003Ccode class=\"language-java hljs\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-function\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Epublic\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Evoid\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-title\"\u003Eathlete\u003C/span\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-params\"\u003E()\u003C/span\u003E \u003C/span\u003E{\nString athleteName;\n\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Edouble\u003C/span\u003E athleteSpeed;\n\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eint\u003C/span\u003E athleteAge;\n}\u003C/code\u003E\u003C/pre\u003E\u003Cfigure class=\"image image_resized\" style=\"width:75%;\"\u003E\u003Cimg data-src=\"https://s3.ap-south-1.amazonaws.com/myinterviewtrainer-domestic/public_assets/assets/000/000/321/original/instance_vs_local_variable.png?1618931277\" \u003C/div\u003E\n\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"what-are-the-default-values-assigned-to-variables-and-instances-in-java\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E8. What are the default values assigned to variables and instances in java?\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cul\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EThere are no default values assigned to the variables in java. We need to initialize the value before using it. Otherwise, it will throw a compilation error of (\u003Cstrong\u003EVariable might not be initialized\u003C/strong\u003E). \u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EBut for instance, if we create the object, then the default value will be initialized by the default constructor depending on the data type. \u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EIf it is a reference, then it will be assigned to null. \u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EIf it is numeric, then it will assign to 0.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EIf it is a boolean, then it will be assigned to false. Etc.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003C/ul\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"what-is-data-encapsulation\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E9. What do you mean by data encapsulation?\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cul\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EData Encapsulation is an Object-Oriented Programming concept of hiding the data attributes and their behaviours in a single unit.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EIt helps developers to follow modularity while developing software by ensuring that each object is independent of other objects by having its own methods, attributes, and functionalities.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EIt is used for the security of the private properties of an object and hence serves the purpose of data hiding.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003C/ul\u003E\u003Cfigure class=\"image image_resized\" style=\"width:75%;\"\u003E\u003Cimg data-src=\"https://s3.ap-south-1.amazonaws.com/myinterviewtrainer-domestic/public_assets/assets/000/000/343/original/data_encapsulation_%281%29.jpg?1619011002\" class=\"lazy-elem\"\u003E\u003C/figure\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"just-in-time-compiler-explained\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E10. Tell us something about JIT compiler.\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cul\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EJIT stands for Just-In-Time and it is used for improving the performance during run time. It does the task of compiling parts of byte code having similar functionality at the same time thereby reducing the amount of compilation time for the code to run.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EThe compiler is nothing but a translator of source code to machine-executable code. But what is special about the JIT compiler? Let us see how it works:\u003Cul\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EFirst, the Java source code (.java) conversion to byte code (.class) occurs with the help of the javac compiler.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EThen, the .class files are loaded at run time by JVM and with the help of an interpreter, these are converted to machine understandable code.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EJIT compiler is a part of JVM. When the JIT compiler is enabled, the JVM analyzes the method calls in the .class files and compiles them to get more efficient and native code. It also ensures that the prioritized method calls are optimized.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EOnce the above step is done, the JVM executes the optimized code directly instead of interpreting the code again. This increases the performance and speed of the execution.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003C/ul\u003E\n\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003C/ul\u003E\u003Cfigure class=\"image image_resized\" style=\"width:75%;\"\u003E\u003Cimg data-src=\"https://s3.ap-south-1.amazonaws.com/myinterviewtrainer-domestic/public_assets/assets/000/000/344/original/JIT_Compiler.jpg?1619011481\" class=\"lazy-elem\"\u003E\u003C/figure\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"difference-between-equality-operator-and-equals-method-java\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E11. Can you tell the difference between equals() method and equality operator (==) in Java?\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cp\u003EWe are already aware of the \u003Cstrong\u003E(==) equals\u003C/strong\u003E operator. That we have used this to compare the equality of the values. But when we talk about the terms of object-oriented programming, we deal with the values in the form of objects. And this object may contain multiple types of data. So using the \u003Cstrong\u003E(==) operator\u003C/strong\u003E does not work in this case. So we need to go with the .\u003Cstrong\u003Eequals() method.\u003C/strong\u003E\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cp\u003EBoth \u003Cstrong\u003E[(==)\u003C/strong\u003E and \u003Cstrong\u003E.equals()]\u003C/strong\u003E primary functionalities are to compare the values, but the secondary functionality is different. \u003C/p\u003E\u003Cp\u003ESo in order to understand this better, lets consider this with the example -\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cpre\u003E\u003Ccode class=\"language-java hljs\"\u003EString str1 = \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003E\"InterviewBit\"\u003C/span\u003E;\nString str2 = \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003E\"InterviewBit\"\u003C/span\u003E;\n \nSystem.out.println(str1 == str2);\u003C/code\u003E\u003C/pre\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThis code will print true. We know that both strings are equals so it will print true. But here \u003Cstrong\u003E(==) Operators\u003C/strong\u003E dont compare each character in this case. It compares the memory location. And because the string uses the constant pool for storing the values in the memory, both \u003Cstrong\u003Estr1\u003C/strong\u003E and \u003Cstrong\u003Estr2\u003C/strong\u003E are stored at the same memory location. See the detailed Explanation in Question no 73: \u003Ca href=\"https://www.interviewbit.com/java-interview-questions/#string-literal-vs-new-string-object-in-java\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"\"\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003ELink\u003C/strong\u003E\u003C/a\u003E.\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cfigure class=\"image image_resized\" style=\"width:75%;\"\u003E\u003Cimg data-src=\"https://d3n0h9tb65y8q.cloudfront.net/public_assets/assets/000/003/688/original/Image-01.png?1663927825\" class=\"lazy-elem\"\u003E\u003C/figure\u003E\u003Cp\u003ENow, if we modify the program a little bit with -\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cpre\u003E\u003Ccode class=\"language-java hljs\"\u003EString str1 = \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Enew\u003C/span\u003E String(\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003E\"InterviewBit\"\u003C/span\u003E);\nString str2 = \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003E\"InterviewBit\"\u003C/span\u003E;\n \nSystem.out.println(str1 == str2);\u003C/code\u003E\u003C/pre\u003E\u003Cfigure class=\"image image_resized\" style=\"width:75%;\"\u003E\u003Cimg data-src=\"https://d3n0h9tb65y8q.cloudfront.net/public_assets/assets/000/003/686/original/Image-02.png?1663927787\" class=\"lazy-elem\"\u003E\u003C/figure\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThen in this case, it will print false. Because here no longer the constant pool concepts are used. Here, new memory is allocated. So here the memory address is different, therefore ( == ) Operator returns false. But the twist is that the values are the same in both strings. So how to compare the values? Here the .equals() method is used.\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003E.equals()\u003C/strong\u003E method compares the values and returns the result accordingly. If we modify the above code with - \u003C/p\u003E\u003Cpre\u003E\u003Ccode class=\"language-java hljs\"\u003ESystem.out.println(str1.equals(str2));\u003C/code\u003E\u003C/pre\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThen it returns true.\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cfigure class=\"table\"\u003E\u003Ctable\u003E\n\u003Cthead\u003E\u003Ctr\u003E\n\u003Cth\u003Eequals() \u003C/th\u003E\n\u003Cth\u003E==\u003C/th\u003E\n\u003C/tr\u003E\u003C/thead\u003E\n\u003Ctbody\u003E\n\u003Ctr\u003E\n\u003Ctd\u003EThis is a method defined in the Object class. \u003C/td\u003E\n\u003Ctd\u003EIt is a binary operator in Java.\u003C/td\u003E\n\u003C/tr\u003E\n\u003Ctr\u003E\n\u003Ctd\u003EThe .equals() Method is present in the Object class, so we can override our custom .equals() method in the custom class, for objects comparison.\u003C/td\u003E\n\u003Ctd\u003EIt cannot be modified. They always compare the HashCode.\u003C/td\u003E\n\u003C/tr\u003E\n\u003Ctr\u003E\n\u003Ctd\u003EThis method is used for checking the equality of contents between two objects as per the specified business logic.\u003C/td\u003E\n\u003Ctd\u003EThis operator is used for comparing addresses (or references), i.e checks if both the objects are pointing to the same memory location.\u003C/td\u003E\n\u003C/tr\u003E\n\u003C/tbody\u003E\n\u003C/table\u003E\u003C/figure\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003ENote:\u003C/strong\u003E\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cul\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EIn the cases where the equals method is not overridden in a class, then the class uses the default implementation of the equals method that is closest to the parent class.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EObject class is considered as the parent class of all the java classes. The implementation of the equals method in the Object class uses the == operator to compare two objects. This default implementation can be overridden as per the business logic.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003C/ul\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"infinite-loops-in-java\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E12. \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"method-overloading-and-overriding-in-java-with-example\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E16. Comment on method overloading and overriding by citing relevant examples.\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cp\u003EIn Java, \u003Cstrong\u003Emethod overloading\u003C/strong\u003E is made possible by introducing different methods in the same class consisting of the same name. Still, all the functions differ in the number or type of parameters. It takes place inside a class and enhances program readability.\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThe only difference in the return type of the method does not promote method overloading. The following example will furnish you with a clear picture of it.\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cpre\u003E\u003Ccode class=\"language-java hljs\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-class\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eclass\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-title\"\u003EOverloadingHelp\u003C/span\u003E \u003C/span\u003E{\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-function\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Epublic\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eint\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-title\"\u003Efindarea\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-params\"\u003E(\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eint\u003C/span\u003E l, \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eint\u003C/span\u003E b)\u003C/span\u003E \u003C/span\u003E{\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eint\u003C/span\u003E var1;\n var1 = l * b;\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Ereturn\u003C/span\u003E var1;\n }\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-function\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Epublic\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eint\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-title\"\u003Efindarea\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-params\"\u003E(\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eint\u003C/span\u003E l, \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eint\u003C/span\u003E b, \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eint\u003C/span\u003E h)\u003C/span\u003E \u003C/span\u003E{\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eint\u003C/span\u003E var2;\n var2 = l * b * h;\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Ereturn\u003C/span\u003E var2;\n }\n}\u003C/code\u003E\u003C/pre\u003E\u003Cfigure class=\"image image_resized\" style=\"width:75%;\"\u003E\u003Cimg data-src=\"https://s3.ap-south-1.amazonaws.com/myinterviewtrainer-domestic/public_assets/assets/000/000/326/original/method_overloading.png?1618932802\" class=\"lazy-elem\"\u003E\u003C/figure\u003E\u003Cp\u003EBoth the functions have the same name but differ in the number of arguments. The first method calculates the area of the rectangle, whereas the second method calculates the area of a cuboid.\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EMethod overriding\u003C/strong\u003E is the concept in which two methods having the same method signature are present in two different classes in which an inheritance relationship is present. A particular method implementation (already present in the base class) is possible for the derived class by using method overriding.\u003Cbr\u003ELets give a look at this A single try block and multiple catch blocks can co-exist in a Java Program. Explain.\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cp\u003EYes, multiple catch blocks can exist but specific approaches should come prior to the general approach because only the first catch block satisfying the catch condition is executed. The given code illustrates the same:\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cpre\u003E\u003Ccode class=\"language-java hljs\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Epublic\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-class\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eclass\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-title\"\u003EMultipleCatch\u003C/span\u003E \u003C/span\u003E{\n\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-function\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Epublic\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Estatic\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Evoid\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-title\"\u003Emain\u003C/span\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-params\"\u003E(String args[])\u003C/span\u003E \u003C/span\u003E{\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Etry\u003C/span\u003E {\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eint\u003C/span\u003E n = \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-number\"\u003E1000\u003C/span\u003E, x = \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-number\"\u003E0\u003C/span\u003E;\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eint\u003C/span\u003E arr[] = \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Enew\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eint\u003C/span\u003E[n];\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Efor\u003C/span\u003E (\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eint\u003C/span\u003E i = \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-number\"\u003E0\u003C/span\u003E; i <= n; i++) {\n arr[i] = i / x;\n }\n }\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Ecatch\u003C/span\u003E (ArrayIndexOutOfBoundsException exception) {\n System.out.println(\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003E\"1st block = ArrayIndexOutOfBoundsException\"\u003C/span\u003E);\n }\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Ecatch\u003C/span\u003E (ArithmeticException exception) {\n System.out.println(\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003E\"2nd block = ArithmeticException\"\u003C/span\u003E);\n }\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Ecatch\u003C/span\u003E (Exception exception) {\n System.out.println(\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003E\"3rd block = Exception\"\u003C/span\u003E);\n }\n}\n}\u003C/code\u003E\u003C/pre\u003E\u003Cp\u003EHere, the second catch block will be executed because of division by 0 (i / x). In case x was greater than 0 then the first catch block will execute because for loop runs till i = n and array index are till n-1.\u003C/p\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"final-keyword-in-java\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E18. Explain the use of final keyword in variable, method and class.\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cp\u003EIn Java, the final keyword is used as defining something as constant /final and represents the non-access modifier.\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cul\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cstrong\u003Efinal variable:\u003C/strong\u003E\u003Cul\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EWhen a variable is declared as final in Java, the value cant be modified once it has been assigned.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EIf any value has not been assigned to that variable, then it can be assigned only by the constructor of the class.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003C/ul\u003E\n\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cstrong\u003Efinal method:\u003C/strong\u003E\u003Cul\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EA method declared as final cannot be overridden by its children's classes.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EA constructor cannot be marked as final because whenever a class is inherited, the constructors are not inherited. Hence, marking it final doesn't make sense. Java throws compilation error saying - \u003Ccode\u003Emodifier final not allowed here\u003C/code\u003E\n\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003C/ul\u003E\n\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cstrong\u003Efinal class:\u003C/strong\u003E\u003Cul\u003E\u003Cli\u003ENo classes can be inherited from the class declared as final. But that final class can extend other classes for its usage.\u003C/li\u003E\u003C/ul\u003E\n\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003C/ul\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"difference-between-final-finally-and-finalize\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E19. Do final, finally and finalize keywords have the same function?\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cp\u003EAll three keywords have their own utility while programming.\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EFinal:\u003C/strong\u003E If any restriction is required for classes, variables, or methods, the final keyword comes in handy. Inheritance of a final class and overriding of a final method is restricted by the use of the final keyword. The variable value becomes fixed after incorporating the final keyword. Example:\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cpre\u003E\u003Ccode class=\"language-java hljs\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Efinal\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eint\u003C/span\u003E a=\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-number\"\u003E100\u003C/span\u003E;\na = \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-number\"\u003E0\u003C/span\u003E; \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-comment\"\u003E// error\u003C/span\u003E\u003C/code\u003E\u003C/pre\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThe second statement will throw an error.\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EFinally:\u003C/strong\u003E It is the block present in a program where all the codes written inside it get executed irrespective of handling of exceptions. Example:\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cpre\u003E\u003Ccode class=\"language-java hljs\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Etry\u003C/span\u003E {\n\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eint\u003C/span\u003E variable = \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-number\"\u003E5\u003C/span\u003E;\n}\n\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Ecatch\u003C/span\u003E (Exception exception) {\nSystem.out.println(\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003E\"Exception occurred\"\u003C/span\u003E);\n}\n\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Efinally\u003C/span\u003E {\nSystem.out.println(\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003E\"Execution of finally block\"\u003C/span\u003E);\n}\u003C/code\u003E\u003C/pre\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EFinalize:\u003C/strong\u003E Prior to the garbage collection of an object, the finalize method is called so that the clean-up activity is implemented. Example:\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cpre\u003E\u003Ccode class=\"language-java hljs\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-function\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Epublic\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Estatic\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Evoid\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-title\"\u003Emain\u003C/span\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-params\"\u003E(String[] args)\u003C/span\u003E \u003C/span\u003E{\nString example = \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Enew\u003C/span\u003E String(\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003E\"InterviewBit\"\u003C/span\u003E);\nexample = \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Enull\u003C/span\u003E;\nSystem.gc(); \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-comment\"\u003E// Garbage collector called\u003C/span\u003E\n}\n\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-function\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Epublic\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Evoid\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-title\"\u003Efinalize\u003C/span\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-params\"\u003E()\u003C/span\u003E \u003C/span\u003E{\n\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-comment\"\u003E// Finalize called\u003C/span\u003E\n} \u003C/code\u003E\u003C/pre\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"is-it-possible-that-the-finally-block-will-not-be-executed-if-yes-then-list-the-case\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E20. class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"can-we-overload-static-methods\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E23. Can the static methods be overloaded?\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cp\u003EYes! There can be two or more static methods in a class with the same name but differing input parameters.\u003C/p\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"why-is-the-main-method-static-in-java\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E24. Why is the main method static in Java?\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cp\u003EThe main method is always static because static members are those methods that belong to the classes, not to an individual object. So if the main method will not be static then for every object, It is available. And that is not acceptable by JVM. JVM calls the main method based on the class name itself. Not by creating the object.\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cp\u003EBecause there must be only 1 main method in the java program as the execution starts from the main method. So for this reason the main method is static. \u003C/p\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"can-static-methods-be-overridden\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E25. Can the static methods be overridden?\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cul\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003ENo! Declaration of static methods having the same signature can be done in the subclass but run time polymorphism can not take place in such cases.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EOverriding or dynamic polymorphism occurs during the runtime, but the static methods are loaded and looked up at the compile time statically. Hence, these methods cant be overridden.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003C/ul\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"static-methods-static-variables-and-static-classes-in-java\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E26. Difference between static methods, static variables, and static classes in java.\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cul\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cstrong\u003EStatic Methods and Static variables\u003C/strong\u003E are those methods and variables that belong to the class of the java program, not to the object of the class. This gets memory where the class is loaded. And these can directly be called with the help of class names.\u003Cul\u003E\u003Cli\u003EFor example - We have used mathematical functions in the java program like - max(), min(), sqrt(), pow(), etc. And if we notice that, then we will find that we call it directly with the class name. Like - Math.max(), Math.min(), etc. So that is a static method. And Similarly static variables we have used like (length) for the array to get the length. So that is the static method.\u003C/li\u003E\u003C/ul\u003E\n\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cstrong\u003EStatic classes \u003C/strong\u003E- A class in the java program cannot be static except if it is the inner class. If it is an inner static class, then it exactly works like other static members of the class.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003C/ul\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"main-objective-of-java-garbage-collection\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E27. What is the main objective of garbage collection?\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cp\u003EThe main objective of this process is to free up the memory space occupied by the unnecessary and unreachable objects during the Java program execution by deleting those unreachable objects.\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cul\u003E\u003Cli\u003EThis ensures that the memory resource is used efficiently, but it provides no guarantee that there would be sufficient memory for the program execution.\u003C/li\u003E\u003C/ul\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"what-is-a-classloader\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E28. What is a ClassLoader?\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cul\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EJava Classloader is the program that belongs to JRE (Java Runtime Environment). The task of ClassLoader is to load the required classes and interfaces to the JVM when required. \u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cstrong\u003EExample-\u003C/strong\u003E To get input from the console, we require the scanner class. And the Scanner class is loaded by the ClassLoader.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003C/ul\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"does-garbage-collector-clean-stack-or-heap\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E29. What part of memory - Stack or Heap - is cleaned in garbage collection process?\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cp\u003EHeap.\u003C/p\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"what-are-shallow-copy-and-deep-copy-in-java\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E30. What are shallow copy and deep copy in java?\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cp\u003ETo copy the object's data, we have several methods like deep copy and shallow copy. \u003C/p\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EExample - \u003C/strong\u003E\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cpre\u003E\u003Ccode class=\"language-java hljs\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-class\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eclass\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-title\"\u003ERectangle\u003C/span\u003E\u003C/span\u003E{\n\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eint\u003C/span\u003E length = \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-number\"\u003E5\u003C/span\u003E;\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eint\u003C/span\u003E breadth = \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-number\"\u003E3\u003C/span\u003E;\n}\u003C/code\u003E\u003C/pre\u003E\u003Cp\u003EObject for this Rectangle class - \u003Cstrong\u003ERectangle obj1 = new Rectangle();\u003C/strong\u003E\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cul\u003E\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cstrong\u003EShallow copy\u003C/strong\u003E - The shallow copy only creates a new reference and points to the same object. Example - For Shallow copy, we can do this by -\u003C/li\u003E\u003C/ul\u003E\u003Cpre\u003E\u003Ccode class=\"language-java hljs\"\u003ERectangle obj2 = obj1;\u003C/code\u003E\u003C/pre\u003E\u003Cp\u003ENow by doing this what will happen is the new reference is created with the name obj2 and that will point to the same memory location.\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cul\u003E\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cstrong\u003EDeep Copy\u003C/strong\u003E - In a deep copy, we create a new object and copy the old object value to the new object. Example -\u003C/li\u003E\u003C/ul\u003E\u003Cpre\u003E\u003Ccode class=\"language-java hljs\"\u003ERectangle obj3 = \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Enew\u003C/span\u003E Rectangle();\nObj3.length = obj1.length;\nObj3.breadth = obj1.breadth;\u003C/code\u003E\u003C/pre\u003E\u003Cp\u003EBoth these objects will point to the memory location as stated below -\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cfigure class=\"image image_resized\" style=\"width:75%;\"\u003E\u003Cimg data-src=\"https://d3n0h9tb65y8q.cloudfront.net/public_assets/assets/000/003/023/original/both_objects_will_point_to_the_memory_location.png?1648813993\" class=\"lazy-elem\"\u003E\u003C/figure\u003E\u003Cp\u003ENow, if we change the values in shallow copy then they affect the other reference as well. Let's see with the help of an example - \u003C/p\u003E\u003Cpre\u003E\u003Ccode class=\"language-java hljs\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-class\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eclass\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-title\"\u003ERectangle\u003C/span\u003E\n\u003C/span\u003E{\n\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eint\u003C/span\u003E length = \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-number\"\u003E5\u003C/span\u003E;\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eint\u003C/span\u003E breadth = \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-number\"\u003E3\u003C/span\u003E;\n}\n\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Epublic\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-class\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eclass\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-title\"\u003EMain\u003C/span\u003E\n\u003C/span\u003E{\n\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-function\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Epublic\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Estatic\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Evoid\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-title\"\u003Emain\u003C/span\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-params\"\u003E(String[] args)\u003C/span\u003E \u003C/span\u003E{\n Rectangle obj1 = \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Enew\u003C/span\u003E Rectangle();\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-comment\"\u003E//Shallow Copy\u003C/span\u003E\n Rectangle obj2 = obj1;\n \n System.out.println(\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003E\" Before Changing the value of object 1, the object2 will be - \"\u003C/span\u003E);\n System.out.println(\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003E\" Object2 Length = \"\u003C/span\u003E+obj2.length+\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003E\", Object2 Breadth = \"\u003C/span\u003E+obj2.breadth);\n \n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-comment\"\u003E//Changing the values for object1.\u003C/span\u003E\n obj1.length = \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-number\"\u003E10\u003C/span\u003E;\n obj1.breadth = \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-number\"\u003E20\u003C/span\u003E;\n \n System.out.println(\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003E\"\\n After Changing the value of object 1, the object2 will be - \"\u003C/span\u003E);\n System.out.println(\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003E\" Object2 Length = \"\u003C/span\u003E+obj2.length+\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003E\", Object2 Breadth = \"\u003C/span\u003E+obj2.breadth);\n \n}\n}\u003C/code\u003E\u003C/pre\u003E\u003Cp\u003EOutput -\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cpre\u003E\u003Ccode class=\"language-java hljs\"\u003EBefore Changing the value of object \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-number\"\u003E1\u003C/span\u003E, the object2 will be - \nObject2 Length = \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-number\"\u003E5\u003C/span\u003E, Object2 Breadth = \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-number\"\u003E3\u003C/span\u003E\n\nAfter Changing the value of object \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-number\"\u003E1\u003C/span\u003E, the object2 will be - \nObject2 Length = \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-number\"\u003E10\u003C/span\u003E, Object2 Breadth = \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-number\"\u003E20\u003C/span\u003E\u003C/code\u003E\u003C/pre\u003E\u003Cp\u003EWe can see that in the above code, if we change the values of object1, then the object2 values also get changed. It is because of the reference.\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cp\u003ENow, if we change the code to deep copy, then there will be no effect on object2 if it is of type deep copy. Consider some snippets to be added in the above code.\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cpre\u003E\u003Ccode class=\"language-java hljs\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-class\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eclass\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-title\"\u003ERectangle\u003C/span\u003E\n\u003C/span\u003E{\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eint\u003C/span\u003E length = \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-number\"\u003E5\u003C/span\u003E;\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eint\u003C/span\u003E breadth = \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-number\"\u003E3\u003C/span\u003E;\n}\n\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Epublic\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-class\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eclass\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-title\"\u003EMain\u003C/span\u003E\n\u003C/span\u003E{\n\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-function\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Epublic\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Estatic\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Evoid\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-title\"\u003Emain\u003C/span\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-params\"\u003E(String[] args)\u003C/span\u003E \u003C/span\u003E{\n Rectangle obj1 = \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Enew\u003C/span\u003E Rectangle();\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-comment\"\u003E//Shallow Copy\u003C/span\u003E\n Rectangle obj2 = \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Enew\u003C/span\u003E Rectangle();\n obj2.length = obj1.length;\n obj2.breadth = obj1.breadth;\n \n System.out.println(\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003E\" Before Changing the value of object 1, the object2 will be - \"\u003C/span\u003E);\n System.out.println(\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003E\" Object2 Length = \"\u003C/span\u003E+obj2.length+\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003E\", Object2 Breadth = \"\u003C/span\u003E+obj2.breadth);\n \n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-comment\"\u003E//Changing the values for object1.\u003C/span\u003E\n obj1.length = \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-number\"\u003E10\u003C/span\u003E;\n obj1.breadth = \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-number\"\u003E20\u003C/span\u003E;\n \n System.out.println(\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003E\"\\n After Changing the value of object 1, the object2 will be - \"\u003C/span\u003E);\n System.out.println(\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003E\" Object2 Length = \"\u003C/span\u003E+obj2.length+\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003E\", Object2 Breadth = \"\u003C/span\u003E+obj2.breadth);\n \n}\n}\u003C/code\u003E\u003C/pre\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThe above snippet will not affect the object2 values. It has its separate values. The output will be\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cpre\u003E\u003Ccode class=\"language-java hljs\"\u003EBefore Changing the value of object \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-number\"\u003E1\u003C/span\u003E, the object2 will be - \nObject2 Length = \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-number\"\u003E5\u003C/span\u003E, Object2 Breadth = \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-number\"\u003E3\u003C/span\u003E\n\nAfter Changing the value of object \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-number\"\u003E1\u003C/span\u003E, the object2 will be - \nObject2 Length = \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-number\"\u003E5\u003C/span\u003E, Object2 Breadth = \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-number\"\u003E3\u003C/span\u003E\u003C/code\u003E\u003C/pre\u003E\u003Cp\u003ENow we see that we need to write the number of codes for this deep copy. So to reduce this, In java, there is a method called \u003Cstrong\u003Eclone().\u003C/strong\u003E \u003C/p\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThe \u003Cstrong\u003Eclone()\u003C/strong\u003E will do this deep copy internally and return a new object. And to do this we need to write only 1 line of code. That is - \u003Cstrong\u003ERectangle obj2 = obj1.clone();\u003C/strong\u003E\u003C/p\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n\n \u003C/div\u003E\n \u003Cdiv\n data-scroll-id=\"1\"\n data-scroll-identifier=\"each-article-section\"\n id=\"intermediate\"\n \u003E\n \u003Ch2\u003EJava Intermediate Interview Questions\u003C/h2\u003E\n\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"reasons-behind-making-strings-immutable-in-java\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E1. Apart from the security aspect, what are the reasons behind making strings immutable in Java?\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cp\u003EA String is made immutable due to the following reasons:\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cul\u003E\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cstrong\u003EString Pool:\u003C/strong\u003E Designers of Java were aware of the fact that String data type is going to be majorly used by the programmers and developers. Thus, they wanted optimization from the beginning. They came up with the notion of using the String pool (a storage area in Java heap) to store the String literals. They intended to decrease the temporary String object with the help of sharing. An immutable class is needed to facilitate sharing. The sharing of the mutable structures between two unknown parties is not possible. Thus, immutable Java String helps in executing the concept of String Pool.\u003C/li\u003E\u003C/ul\u003E\u003Cfigure class=\"image image_resized\" style=\"width:75%;\"\u003E\u003Cimg data-src=\"https://s3.ap-south-1.amazonaws.com/myinterviewtrainer-domestic/public_assets/assets/000/000/335/original/string_pool.png?1618995310\" class=\"lazy-elem\"\u003E\u003C/figure\u003E\u003Cul\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Ca href=\"https://www.interviewbit.com/multithreading-interview-questions/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"\"\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EMultithreading\u003C/strong\u003E\u003C/a\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003E:\u003C/strong\u003E The safety of threads regarding the String objects is an important aspect in Java. No external synchronization is required if the String objects are immutable. Thus, a cleaner code can be written for sharing the String objects across different threads. The complex process of concurrency is facilitated by this method.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Ca href=\"https://www.interviewbit.com/java-collections-interview-questions/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"\"\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003ECollections\u003C/strong\u003E\u003C/a\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003E:\u003C/strong\u003E In the case of Hashtables and HashMaps, keys are String objects. If the String objects are not immutable, then it can get modified during the period when it resides in the HashMaps. Consequently, the retrieval of the desired data is not possible. Such changing states pose a lot of risks. Therefore, it is quite safe to make the string immutable.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003C/ul\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"what-is-a-singleton-class-in-java-how-to-implement-a-singleton-class\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E2. What is a singleton class in Java? And How to implement a singleton class?\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cp\u003ESingleton classes are those classes, whose objects are created only once. And with only that object the class members can be accessed. \u003C/p\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EUnderstand this with the help of an example-:\u003C/strong\u003E\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cp\u003EConsider the water jug in the office and if every employee wants that water then they will not create a new water jug for drinking water. They will use the existing one with their own reference as a glass. So programmatically it should be implemented as -\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cpre\u003E\u003Ccode class=\"language-java hljs\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-class\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eclass\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-title\"\u003EWaterJug\u003C/span\u003E\u003C/span\u003E{\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eprivate\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eint\u003C/span\u003E waterQuantity = \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-number\"\u003E500\u003C/span\u003E;\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-function\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eprivate\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-title\"\u003EWaterJug\u003C/span\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-params\"\u003E()\u003C/span\u003E\u003C/span\u003E{}\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eprivate\u003C/span\u003E WaterJug object = \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Enull\u003C/span\u003E;\n \n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-comment\"\u003E// Method to provide the service of Giving Water.\u003C/span\u003E\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-function\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Epublic\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eint\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-title\"\u003EgetWater\u003C/span\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-params\"\u003E(\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eint\u003C/span\u003E quantity)\u003C/span\u003E\u003C/span\u003E{\n waterQuantity -= quantity;\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Ereturn\u003C/span\u003E quantity;\n }\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-comment\"\u003E// Method to return the object to the user.\u003C/span\u003E\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-function\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Epublic\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Estatic\u003C/span\u003E Waterjug \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-title\"\u003EgetInstance\u003C/span\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-params\"\u003E()\u003C/span\u003E\u003C/span\u003E{\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-comment\"\u003E// Will Create a new object if the object is not already created and return the object.\u003C/span\u003E\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eif\u003C/span\u003E(object == \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Enull\u003C/span\u003E){\n object = \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Enew\u003C/span\u003E WaterJug();\n }\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Ereturn\u003C/span\u003E object;\n }\n}\u003C/code\u003E\u003C/pre\u003E\u003Cp\u003EIn the above class, the Constructor is private so we cannot create the object of the class. But we can get the object by calling the method \u003Cstrong\u003EgetInstance()\u003C/strong\u003E. And the getInstance is static so it can be called without creating the object. And it returns the object. Now with that object, we can call \u003Cstrong\u003EgetWater() \u003C/strong\u003Eto get the water.\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cpre\u003E\u003Ccode class=\"language-java hljs\"\u003EWaterjug glass1 = WaterJug.getInstance();\nglass1.getWater(\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-number\"\u003E1\u003C/span\u003E);\u003C/code\u003E\u003C/pre\u003E\u003Cp\u003EWe can get the single object using this getInstance(). And it is static, so it is a thread-safe singleton class. Although there are many ways to create a thread-safe singleton class. So thread-safe classes can also be:\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cul\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EWhen singletons are written with double-checked locking, they can be thread-safe.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EWe can use static singletons that are initialized during class loading. Like we did in the above example.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EBut the most straightforward way to create a thread-safe singleton is to use Java enums.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003C/ul\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"which-of-the-below-generates-a-compile-time-error-state-the-reason\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E3. Which of the below generates a compile-time error? State the reason. \u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Col\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003Eint[] n1 = new int[0];\u003C/strong\u003E\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003Eboolean[] n2 = new boolean[-200];\u003C/strong\u003E\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003Edouble[] n3 = new double[2241423798];\u003C/strong\u003E\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003Echar[] ch = new char[20];\u003C/strong\u003E\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003C/ol\u003E\u003Cp\u003EWe get a compile-time error in line 3. The error we will get in Line 3 is - \u003Cstrong\u003Einteger number too large\u003C/strong\u003E. It is because the array requires size as an integer. And Integer takes 4 Bytes in the memory. And the number (\u003Cstrong\u003E2241423798\u003C/strong\u003E) is beyond the capacity of the integer. The maximum array size we can declare is - (\u003Cstrong\u003E2147483647\u003C/strong\u003E).\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cp\u003EBecause the array requires the size in integer, none of the lines (1, 2, and 4) will give a compile-time error. The program will compile fine. But we get the runtime exception in line 2. The exception is - \u003Cstrong\u003ENegativeArraySizeException\u003C/strong\u003E. \u003C/p\u003E\u003Cp\u003EHere what will happen is - At the time when JVM will allocate the required memory during runtime then it will find that the size is negative. And the array size cant be negative. So the JVM will throw the exception.\u003C/p\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"string-vs-stringbuffer-vs-stringbuilder-in-java\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E4. How would you differentiate between a String, StringBuffer, and a StringBuilder?\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cul\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cstrong\u003EStorage area:\u003C/strong\u003E In string, the String pool serves as the storage area. For StringBuilder and StringBuffer, heap memory is the storage area.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cstrong\u003EMutability:\u003C/strong\u003E A String is immutable, whereas both the StringBuilder and StringBuffer are mutable.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cstrong\u003EEfficiency:\u003C/strong\u003E It is quite slow to work with a String. However, StringBuilder is the fastest in performing operations. The speed of a StringBuffer is more than a String and less than a StringBuilder. (For example appending a character is fastest in StringBuilder and very slow in String because a new memory is required for the new String with appended character.)\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cstrong\u003EThread-safe:\u003C/strong\u003E In the case of a threaded environment, StringBuilder and StringBuffer are used whereas a String is not used. However, StringBuilder is suitable for an environment with a single thread, and a StringBuffer is suitable for multiple threads.\u003Cbr\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003ESyntax:\u003C/strong\u003E\n\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003C/ul\u003E\u003Cpre\u003E\u003Ccode class=\"language-java hljs\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-comment\"\u003E// String\u003C/span\u003E\nString first = \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003E\"InterviewBit\"\u003C/span\u003E;\nString second = \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Enew\u003C/span\u003E String(\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003E\"InterviewBit\"\u003C/span\u003E);\n\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-comment\"\u003E// StringBuffer\u003C/span\u003E\nStringBuffer third = \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Enew\u003C/span\u003E StringBuffer(\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003E\"InterviewBit\"\u003C/span\u003E);\n\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-comment\"\u003E// StringBuilder\u003C/span\u003E\nStringBuilder fourth = \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Enew\u003C/span\u003E StringBuilder(\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003E\"InterviewBit\"\u003C/span\u003E);\u003C/code\u003E\u003C/pre\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"difference-between-abstract-classses-and-interfaces\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E5. Using relevant properties highlight the differences between interfaces and abstract classes.\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cul\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cstrong\u003EAvailability of methods:\u003C/strong\u003E Only abstract methods are available in interfaces, whereas non-abstract methods can be present along with abstract methods in abstract classes.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cstrong\u003EVariable types\u003C/strong\u003E: Static and final variables can only be declared in the case of interfaces, whereas abstract classes can also have non-static and non-final variables.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cstrong\u003EInheritance: \u003C/strong\u003EMultiple inheritances are facilitated by interfaces, whereas abstract classes do not promote multiple inheritances.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cstrong\u003EData member accessibility:\u003C/strong\u003E By default, the class data members of interfaces are of the public- type. Conversely, the class members for an abstract class can be protected or private also.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cstrong\u003EImplementation:\u003C/strong\u003E With the help of an abstract class, the implementation of an interface is easily possible. However, the converse is not true;\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003C/ul\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EAbstract class example:\u003C/strong\u003E\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cpre\u003E\u003Ccode class=\"language-java hljs\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Epublic\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eabstract\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-class\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eclass\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-title\"\u003EAthlete\u003C/span\u003E \u003C/span\u003E{\n\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-function\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Epublic\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eabstract\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Evoid\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-title\"\u003Ewalk\u003C/span\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-params\"\u003E()\u003C/span\u003E\u003C/span\u003E;\n}\u003C/code\u003E\u003C/pre\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EInterface example:\u003C/strong\u003E\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cpre\u003E\u003Ccode class=\"language-java hljs\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Epublic\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-class\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Einterface\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-title\"\u003EWalkable\u003C/span\u003E \u003C/span\u003E{\n\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-function\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Evoid\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-title\"\u003Ewalk\u003C/span\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-params\"\u003E()\u003C/span\u003E\u003C/span\u003E;\n}\u003C/code\u003E\u003C/pre\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"is-this-program-giving-a-compile-time-error-if-yes-then-state-the-reason-and-number-of-errors-it-will-give-if-not-then-state-the-reason\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E6. If not then state the reason.\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cpre\u003E\u003Ccode class=\"language-java hljs\"\u003E\u003Cspan The compiler will throw 2 errors in this.\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cul\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cstrong\u003E[Illegal Combination of modifiers: abstract and final]\u003C/strong\u003E at line 1.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cstrong\u003E[Cannot inherit from final InterviewBit]\u003C/strong\u003E at line 4.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003C/ul\u003E\u003Cp\u003EIt is because abstract classes are incomplete classes that need to be inherited for making their concrete classes. And on the other hand, the final keywords in class are used for avoiding inheritance. So these combinations are not allowed in java.\u003C/p\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"what-is-a-comparator-in-java\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E7. What is a Comparator in java?\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cp\u003EConsider the example where we have an ArrayList of employees like( EId, Ename, Salary), etc. Now if we want to sort this list of employees based on the names of employees. Then that is not possible to sort using the Collections.sort() method. We need to provide something to the sort() function depending on what values we have to perform sorting. Then in that case a comparator is used.\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cp\u003EComparator is the interface in java that contains the compare method. And by overloading the compare method, we can define that on what basis we need to compare the values. \u003C/p\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"can-we-override-a-static-or-private-method-in-java\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E8. In Java, static as well as private method overriding is possible. Comment on the statement.\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cp\u003EThe statement in the context is completely False. The static methods have no relevance with the objects, and these methods are of the class level. In the case of a child class, a static method with a method signature exactly like that of the parent class can exist without even throwing any compilation error.\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThe phenomenon mentioned here is popularly known as method hiding, and overriding is certainly not possible. Private method overriding is unimaginable because the visibility of the private method is restricted to the parent class only. As a result, only hiding can be facilitated and not overriding.\u003C/p\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"hashset-vs-treeset-in-java\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E9. What makes a HashSet different from a TreeSet?\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cp\u003EAlthough both HashSet and TreeSet are not synchronized and ensure that duplicates are not present, there are certain properties that distinguish a HashSet from a TreeSet.\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cul\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cstrong\u003EImplementation:\u003C/strong\u003E For a HashSet, the hash table is utilized for storing the elements in an unordered manner. However, TreeSet makes use of the red-black tree to store the elements in a sorted manner.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cstrong\u003EComplexity/ Performance:\u003C/strong\u003E For adding, retrieving, and deleting elements, the time amortized complexity is O(1) for a HashSet. The time complexity for performing the same operations is a bit higher for TreeSet and is equal to O(log n). Overall, the performance of HashSet is faster in comparison to TreeSet.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cstrong\u003EMethods: \u003C/strong\u003EhashCode() and equals() are the methods utilized by HashSet for making comparisons between the objects. Conversely, compareTo() and compare() methods are utilized by TreeSet to facilitate object comparisons.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cstrong\u003EObjects type:\u003C/strong\u003E Heterogeneous and null objects can be stored with the help of HashSet. In the case of a TreeSet, runtime exception occurs while inserting heterogeneous objects or null objects.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003C/ul\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"why-char-array-preferred-to-store-confidential-data-in-java\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E10. Why is the character array preferred over string for storing confidential information?\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cp\u003EIn Java, a string is basically immutable i.e. it cannot be modified. After its declaration, it continues to stay in the string pool as long as it is not removed in the form of garbage. In other words, a string resides in the heap section of the memory for an unregulated and unspecified time interval after string value processing is executed.\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cp\u003EAs a result, vital information can be stolen for pursuing harmful activities by hackers if a memory dump is illegally accessed by them. Such risks can be eliminated by using mutable objects or structures like character arrays for storing any variable. After the work of the character array variable is done, the variable can be configured to blank at the same instant. Consequently, it helps in saving heap memory and also gives no chance to the hackers to extract vital data.\u003C/p\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"what-do-we-get-in-the-jdk-file\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E11. What do we get in the JDK file?\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cul\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cstrong\u003EJDK\u003C/strong\u003E- For making java programs, we need some tools that are provided by JDK (Java Development Kit). JDK is the package that contains various tools, Compiler, Java Runtime Environment, etc.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cstrong\u003EJRE \u003C/strong\u003E- To execute the java program we need an environment. (Java Runtime Environment) JRE contains a library of Java classes + JVM. \u003Cstrong\u003EWhat are JAVA Classes?\u003C/strong\u003E It contains some predefined methods that help Java programs to use that feature, build and execute. \u003Ci\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EFor example\u003C/strong\u003E\u003C/i\u003E - there is a system class in java that contains the print-stream method, and with the help of this, we can print something on the console.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cstrong\u003EJVM\u003C/strong\u003E - (Java Virtual Machine) JVM is a part of JRE that executes the Java program at the end. Actually, it is part of JRE, but it is software that converts bytecode into machine-executable code to execute on hardware.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003C/ul\u003E\u003Cfigure class=\"image image_resized\" style=\"width:50%;\"\u003E\u003Cimg data-src=\"https://d3n0h9tb65y8q.cloudfront.net/public_assets/assets/000/003/021/original/jdk_jre_jvm.png?1648813873\" class=\"lazy-elem\"\u003E\u003C/figure\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"jvm-vs-jre-vs-jdk-in-java\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E12. What are the differences between JVM, JRE and JDK in Java?\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cfigure class=\"table\"\u003E\u003Ctable\u003E\n\u003Cthead\u003E\u003Ctr\u003E\n\u003Cth\u003ECriteria\u003C/th\u003E\n\u003Cth\u003EJDK \u003C/th\u003E\n\u003Cth\u003EJRE\u003C/th\u003E\n\u003Cth\u003EJVM\u003C/th\u003E\n\u003C/tr\u003E\u003C/thead\u003E\n\u003Ctbody\u003E\n\u003Ctr\u003E\n\u003Cth\u003EAbbreviation\u003C/th\u003E\n\u003Ctd\u003EJava Development Kit\u003C/td\u003E\n\u003Ctd\u003EJava Runtime Environment\u003C/td\u003E\n\u003Ctd\u003EJava Virtual Machine\u003C/td\u003E\n\u003C/tr\u003E\n\u003Ctr\u003E\n\u003Cth\u003EDefinition\u003C/th\u003E\n\u003Ctd\u003EJDK is a complete software development kit for developing Java applications. It comprises JRE, JavaDoc, compiler, debuggers, etc.\u003C/td\u003E\n\u003Ctd\u003EJRE is a software package providing Java class libraries, JVM and all the required components to run the Java applications.\u003C/td\u003E\n\u003Ctd\u003EJVM is a platform-dependent, abstract machine comprising of 3 specifications - document describing the JVM implementation requirements, computer program meeting the JVM requirements and instance object for executing the Java byte code and provide the runtime environment for execution.\u003C/td\u003E\n\u003C/tr\u003E\n\u003Ctr\u003E\n\u003Cth\u003EMain Purpose\u003C/th\u003E\n\u003Ctd\u003EJDK is mainly used for code development and execution.\u003C/td\u003E\n\u003Ctd\u003EJRE is mainly used for environment creation to execute the code.\u003C/td\u003E\n\u003Ctd\u003EJVM provides specifications for all the implementations to JRE.\u003C/td\u003E\n\u003C/tr\u003E\n\u003Ctr\u003E\n\u003Cth\u003ETools provided\u003C/th\u003E\n\u003Ctd\u003EJDK provides tools like compiler, debuggers, etc for code development\u003C/td\u003E\n\u003Ctd\u003EJRE provides libraries and classes required by JVM to run the program.\u003C/td\u003E\n\u003Ctd\u003EJVM does not include any tools, but instead, it provides the specification for implementation.\u003C/td\u003E\n\u003C/tr\u003E\n\u003Ctr\u003E\n\u003Cth\u003ESummary\u003C/th\u003E\n\u003Ctd\u003EJDK = (JRE) + Development tools\u003C/td\u003E\n\u003Ctd\u003EJRE = (JVM) + Libraries to execute the application\u003C/td\u003E\n\u003Ctd\u003EJVM = Runtime environment to execute Java byte code.\u003C/td\u003E\n\u003C/tr\u003E\n\u003C/tbody\u003E\n\u003C/table\u003E\u003C/figure\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"difference-between-hashmap-and-hashtable-in-java\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E13. What are the differences between HashMap and HashTable in Java?\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cfigure class=\"table\"\u003E\u003Ctable\u003E\n\u003Cthead\u003E\u003Ctr\u003E\n\u003Cth\u003EHashMap\u003C/th\u003E\n\u003Cth\u003EHashTable\u003C/th\u003E\n\u003C/tr\u003E\u003C/thead\u003E\n\u003Ctbody\u003E\n\u003Ctr\u003E\n\u003Ctd\u003EHashMap is not synchronized thereby making it better for non-threaded applications.\u003C/td\u003E\n\u003Ctd\u003EHashTable is synchronized and hence it is suitable for threaded applications.\u003C/td\u003E\n\u003C/tr\u003E\n\u003Ctr\u003E\n\u003Ctd\u003EAllows only one null key but any number of null in the values.\u003C/td\u003E\n\u003Ctd\u003EThis does not allow null in both keys or values.\u003C/td\u003E\n\u003C/tr\u003E\n\u003Ctr\u003E\n\u003Ctd\u003ESupports order of insertion by making use of its subclass LinkedHashMap.\u003C/td\u003E\n\u003Ctd\u003EOrder of insertion is not guaranteed in HashTable.\u003C/td\u003E\n\u003C/tr\u003E\n\u003C/tbody\u003E\n\u003C/table\u003E\u003C/figure\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"importance-of-reflection-in-java\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E14. What is the importance of reflection in Java?\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cul\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EThe term \u003Ccode\u003Ereflection\u003C/code\u003E is used for describing the inspection capability of a code on other code either of itself or of its system and modify it during runtime.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EConsider an example where we have an object of unknown type and we have a method fooBar() which we need to call on the object. The static typing system of Java doesn't allow this method invocation unless the type of the object is known beforehand. This can be achieved using reflection which allows the code to scan the object and identify if it has any method called fooBar() and only then call the method if needed.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003C/ul\u003E\u003Cpre\u003E\u003Ccode class=\"language-java hljs\"\u003EMethod methodOfFoo = fooObject.getClass().getMethod(\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003E\"fooBar\"\u003C/span\u003E, \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Enull\u003C/span\u003E);\nmethodOfFoo.invoke(fooObject, \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Enull\u003C/span\u003E);\u003C/code\u003E\u003C/pre\u003E\u003Cul\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EUsing reflection has its own cons:\u003Cul\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003ESpeed Method invocations due to reflection are about three times slower than the direct method calls.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EType safety When a method is invoked via its reference wrongly using reflection, invocation fails at runtime as it is not detected at compile/load time.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003ETraceability Whenever a reflective method fails, it is very difficult to find the root cause of this failure due to a huge stack trace. One has to deep dive into the invoke() and proxy() method logs to identify the root cause.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003C/ul\u003E\n\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EHence, it is advisable to follow solutions that don't involve reflection and use this method as a last resort.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003C/ul\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"different-ways-of-java-threads-usage\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E15. What are the different ways of threads usage?\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cul\u003E\u003Cli\u003EWe can define and implement a thread in java using two ways:\u003Cul\u003E\u003Cli\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EExtending the Thread class\u003C/strong\u003E\u003C/li\u003E\u003C/ul\u003E\n\u003C/li\u003E\u003C/ul\u003E\u003Cpre\u003E\u003Ccode class=\"language-java hljs\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-class\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eclass\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-title\"\u003EInterviewBitThreadExample\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eextends\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-title\"\u003EThread\u003C/span\u003E\u003C/span\u003E{ \n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-function\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Epublic\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Evoid\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-title\"\u003Erun\u003C/span\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-params\"\u003E()\u003C/span\u003E\u003C/span\u003E{ \n System.out.println(\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003E\"Thread runs...\"\u003C/span\u003E); Once the call stack is created, JVM calls the \u003Ccode\u003Erun()\u003C/code\u003E method for executing the thread in that call stack.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003C/ul\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"different-types-of-thread-priorities-in-java-and-default-priority-of-a-thread-assigned-by-jvm\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E16. What are the different types of Thread Priorities in Java? And what is the default priority of a thread assigned by JVM?\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cp\u003EThere are a total of 3 different types of priority available in Java. \u003C/p\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EMIN_PRIORITY:\u003C/strong\u003E It has an integer value assigned with 1.\u003Cbr\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EMAX_PRIORITY:\u003C/strong\u003E It has an integer value assigned with 10.\u003Cbr\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003ENORM_PRIORITY: \u003C/strong\u003EIt has an integer value assigned with 5.\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cp\u003EIn Java, Thread with MAX_PRIORITY gets the first chance to execute. But the default priority for any thread is NORM_PRIORITY assigned by JVM. \u003C/p\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"difference-between-the-program-and-the-process\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E17. What is the difference between the program and the process?\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cul\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EA program can be defined as a line of code written in order to accomplish a particular task. Whereas the process can be defined as the programs which are under execution. \u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EA program doesn't execute directly by the CPU. First, the resources are allocated to the program and when it is ready for execution then it is a process.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003C/ul\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"difference-between-throw-and-throws-keyword-in-java\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E18. What are the differences between constructor and method of a class in Java?\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cfigure class=\"table\"\u003E\u003Ctable\u003E\n\u003Cthead\u003E\u003Ctr\u003E\n\u003Cth\u003EConstructor\u003C/th\u003E\n\u003Cth\u003EMethod\u003C/th\u003E\n\u003C/tr\u003E\u003C/thead\u003E\n\u003Ctbody\u003E\n\u003Ctr\u003E\n\u003Ctd\u003EConstructor is used for initializing the object state.\u003C/td\u003E\n\u003Ctd\u003EMethod is used for exposing the object's behavior.\u003C/td\u003E\n\u003C/tr\u003E\n\u003Ctr\u003E\n\u003Ctd\u003EConstructor has no return type.\u003C/td\u003E\n\u003Ctd\u003EMethod should have a return type.
