Hence, marking it final doesn't make sense. Java throws compilation error saying - \u003Ccode\u003Emodifier final not allowed here\u003C/code\u003E\n\u003C/td\u003E\n\u003Ctd\u003EA method can be defined as final but it cannot be overridden in its subclasses.\u003C/td\u003E\n\u003C/tr\u003E\n\u003Ctr\u003E\n\u003Ctd\u003EFinal variable instantiations are possible inside a constructor and the scope of this applies to the whole class and its objects.\u003C/td\u003E\n\u003Ctd\u003EA final variable if initialised inside a method ensures that the variable cant be changed only within the scope of that method.\u003C/td\u003E\n\u003C/tr\u003E\n\u003C/tbody\u003E\n\u003C/table\u003E\u003C/figure\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"identify-the-output-of-the-below-java-program-and-justify-your-answer\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E20. Java works as pass by value or pass by reference phenomenon?\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cp\u003EJava always works as a pass by value. There is nothing called a pass by reference in Java. However, when the object is passed in any method, the address of the value is passed due to the nature of object handling in Java. When an object is passed, a copy of the reference is created by Java and that is passed to the method. The objects point to the same memory location. 2 cases might happen inside the method:\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cul\u003E\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cstrong\u003ECase 1: \u003C/strong\u003EWhen the object is object.\u003C/li\u003E\u003C/ul\u003E\u003Cp\u003EFor example:\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cpre\u003E\u003Ccode class=\"language-java hljs\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-class\"\u003E\u003Cspan id=\"what-is-the-is-a-relationship-in-oops-java\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E22. What is the IS-A relationship in OOPs java?\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cp\u003EIS-A relationship is another name for inheritance. When we inherit the base class from the derived class, then it forms a relationship between the classes. So that relationship is termed an IS-A Relationship.\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EExample \u003C/strong\u003E- Consider a Television (Typical CRT TV). Now another Smart TV that is inherited from television class. So we can say that the Smart iv is also a TV. Because CRT TV things can also be done in the Smart TV.\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cfigure class=\"image image_resized\" style=\"width:75%;\"\u003E\u003Cimg data-src=\"https://d3n0h9tb65y8q.cloudfront.net/public_assets/assets/000/003/039/original/IS-A_relationship_in_OOPs_java.png?1648817219\" class=\"lazy-elem\"\u003E\u003C/figure\u003E\u003Cp\u003ESo here IS-A Relationship formed. \u003Cstrong\u003E[ SmartTV IS-A TV ]\u003C/strong\u003E.\u003C/p\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"string-or-stringbuffer-is-preferred-when-alot-of-updates-has-to-be-done-in-the-data\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E23. Which among String or String Buffer should be preferred when there are lot of updates required to be done in the data?\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cp\u003EStringBuffer is mutable and dynamic in nature whereas String is immutable. Every updation / modification of String creates a new String thereby overloading the string pool with unnecessary objects. Hence, in the cases of a lot of updates, it is always preferred to use StringBuffer as it will reduce the overhead of the creation of multiple String objects in the string pool.\u003C/p\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"how-to-avoid-serialization-of-attributes-of-a-class-in-java\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E24. How to not allow serialization of attributes of a class in Java?\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cul\u003E\u003Cli\u003EIn order to achieve this, the attribute can be declared along with the usage of \u003Ccode\u003Etransient\u003C/code\u003E keyword as shown below:\u003C/li\u003E\u003C/ul\u003E\u003Cpre\u003E\u003Ccode class=\"language-java hljs\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Epublic\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-class\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eclass\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-title\"\u003EInterviewBitExample\u003C/span\u003E \u003C/span\u003E{ \n\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eprivate\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Etransient\u003C/span\u003E String someInfo; \n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eprivate\u003C/span\u003E String name;\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eprivate\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eint\u003C/span\u003E id;\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-comment\"\u003E// :\u003C/span\u003E\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-comment\"\u003E// Getters setters\u003C/span\u003E\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-comment\"\u003E// :\u003C/span\u003E\n} \u003C/code\u003E\u003C/pre\u003E\u003Cul\u003E\u003Cli\u003EIn the above example, all the fields except \u003Ccode\u003EsomeInfo\u003C/code\u003E can be serialized.\u003C/li\u003E\u003C/ul\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"what-if-the-static-modifier-is-removed-from-the-main-method-signature-in-java\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E25. What happens if the static modifier is not included in the main method signature in Java?\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cp\u003EThere wouldn't be any compilation error. But then the program is run, since the JVM cant map the main method signature, the code throws NoSuchMethodError error at the runtime.\u003C/p\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"consider-the-below-program-identify-the-output-and-also-state-the-reason-for-that\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E26. Consider the below program, identify the output, and also state the reason for that.\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cpre\u003E\u003Ccode class=\"language-java hljs\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Epublic\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-class\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eclass\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-title\"\u003EMain\u003C/span\u003E\u003C/span\u003E{\n\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-function\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Epublic\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Estatic\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Evoid\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-title\"\u003Emain\u003C/span\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-params\"\u003E(String[] args)\u003C/span\u003E \u003C/span\u003E{\n System.out.println(\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003E\" Hello. Main Method. \"\u003C/span\u003E);\n}\n\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-function\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Epublic\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Estatic\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Evoid\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-title\"\u003Emain\u003C/span\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-params\"\u003E(\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eint\u003C/span\u003E[] args)\u003C/span\u003E \u003C/span\u003E{\n System.out.println(\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003E\" Hello. Main Method2. \"\u003C/span\u003E);\n}\n}\u003C/code\u003E\u003C/pre\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThe output of the above program will be \u003Cstrong\u003EHello. Main Method\u003C/strong\u003E. This is because JVM will always call the main method based on the definition it already has. Doesn't matter how many main methods we overload it will only execute one main method based on its declaration in JVM.\u003C/p\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"can-we-make-the-main-thread-a-daemon-thread\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E27. Can we make the main() thread a daemon thread?\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cp\u003EIn java multithreading, the main() threads are always non-daemon threads. And there is no way we can change the nature of the non-daemon thread to the daemon thread.\u003C/p\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"what-happens-if-there-are-multiple-main-methods-inside-one-class-in-java\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E28. What happens if there are multiple main methods inside one class in Java?\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cp\u003EThe program can't compile as the compiler says that the method has been already defined inside the class.\u003C/p\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"object-cloning-in-java\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E29. What do you understand by Object Cloning and how do you achieve it in Java?\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cul\u003E\u003Cli\u003EIt is the process of creating an exact copy of any object. In order to support this, a java class has to implement the Cloneable interface of java.lang package and override the clone() method provided by the Object class the syntax of which is:\u003C/li\u003E\u003C/ul\u003E\u003Cpre\u003E\u003Ccode class=\"language-java hljs\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-function\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eprotected\u003C/span\u003E Object \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-title\"\u003Eclone\u003C/span\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-params\"\u003E()\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Ethrows\u003C/span\u003E CloneNotSupportedException\u003C/span\u003E{\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Ereturn\u003C/span\u003E (Object)\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Esuper\u003C/span\u003E.clone();\n}\u003C/code\u003E\u003C/pre\u003E\u003Cul\u003E\u003Cli\u003EIn case the Cloneable interface is not implemented and just the method is overridden, it results in CloneNotSupportedException in Java.\u003C/li\u003E\u003C/ul\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"exception-propagation-java\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E30. How does an exception propagate in the code?\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cp\u003EWhen an exception occurs, first it searches to locate the matching catch block. In case, the matching catch block is located, then that block would be executed. Else, the exception propagates through the method call stack and goes into the caller method where the process of matching the catch block is performed. This propagation happens until the matching catch block is found. If the match is not found, then the program gets terminated in the main method.\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cfigure class=\"image image_resized\" style=\"width:75%;\"\u003E\u003Cimg data-src=\"https://s3.ap-south-1.amazonaws.com/myinterviewtrainer-domestic/public_assets/assets/000/000/345/original/java_stack.jpg?1619019436\" class=\"lazy-elem\"\u003E\u003C/figure\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"how-do-exceptions-affect-the-program-if-it-doesnt-handle-them\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E31. How do exceptions affect the program if it doesn't handle them?\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cp\u003EExceptions are runtime errors. Suppose we are making an android application with java. And it all works fine but there is an exceptional case when the application tries to get the file from storage and the file doesnt exist (This is the case of exception in java). And if this case is not handled properly then the application will crash. This will be a bad experience for users. This is the type of error that cannot be controlled by the programmer. But programmers can take some steps to avoid this so that the application wont crash. The proper action can be taken at this step.\u003C/p\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"is-it-mandatory-for-a-catch-block-to-be-followed-after-a-try-block-in-java\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E32. Is it mandatory for a catch block to be followed after a try block?\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cp\u003ENo, it is not necessary for a catch block to be present after a try block. - A try block should be followed either by a catch block or by a finally block. If the exceptions likelihood is more, then they should be declared using the throws clause of the method.\u003C/p\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"will-finally-block-get-executed-when-the-return-statement-is-written-at-the-end-of-try-block-and-catch-block\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E33. Will the finally block get executed when the return statement is written at the end of try block and catch block as shown below?\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cpre\u003E\u003Ccode class=\"language-java hljs\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-function\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Epublic\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eint\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-title\"\u003EsomeMethod\u003C/span\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-params\"\u003E(\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eint\u003C/span\u003E i)\u003C/span\u003E\u003C/span\u003E{\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Etry\u003C/span\u003E{\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-comment\"\u003E//some statement\u003C/span\u003E\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Ereturn\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-number\"\u003E1\u003C/span\u003E;\n }\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Ecatch\u003C/span\u003E(Exception e){\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-comment\"\u003E//some statement\u003C/span\u003E\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Ereturn\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-number\"\u003E999\u003C/span\u003E;\n }\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Efinally\u003C/span\u003E{\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-comment\"\u003E//finally block statements\u003C/span\u003E\n }\n}\u003C/code\u003E\u003C/pre\u003E\u003Cp\u003Efinally block will be executed irrespective of the exception or not. The only case where finally block is not executed is when it encounters System.exit() method anywhere in try/catch block.\u003C/p\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"can-a-constructor-of-a-class-inside-another-constructor-be-called-in-java\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E34. Can you call a constructor of a class inside the another constructor?\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cp\u003EYes, the concept can be termed as constructor chaining and can be achieved using \u003Ccode\u003Ethis()\u003C/code\u003E.\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cfigure class=\"image image_resized\" style=\"width:75%;\"\u003E\u003Cimg data-src=\"https://s3.ap-south-1.amazonaws.com/myinterviewtrainer-domestic/public_assets/assets/000/000/346/original/constructor_chaining_in_Java.jpg?1619071959\" class=\"lazy-elem\"\u003E\u003C/figure\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"why-contiguous-memory-locations-store-actual-values-in-array-and-not-in-arraylist\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E35. Contiguous memory locations are usually used for storing actual values in an array but not in ArrayList. Explain.\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cp\u003EIn the case of ArrayList, data storing in the form of primitive data types (like int, float, etc.) is not possible. The data members/objects present in the ArrayList have references to the objects which are located at various sites in the memory. Thus, storing of actual objects or non-primitive data types (like Integer, Double, etc.) takes place in various memory locations.\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cfigure class=\"image image_resized\" style=\"width:75%;\"\u003E\u003Cimg data-src=\"https://s3.ap-south-1.amazonaws.com/myinterviewtrainer-domestic/public_assets/assets/000/000/328/original/sorting_of_objects_in_arraylist.png?1618934804\" class=\"lazy-elem\"\u003E\u003C/figure\u003E\u003Cp\u003EHowever, the same does not apply to the arrays. Object or primitive type values can be stored in arrays in contiguous memory locations, hence every element does not require any reference to the next element.\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cfigure class=\"image image_resized\" style=\"width:75%;\"\u003E\u003Cimg data-src=\"https://s3.ap-south-1.amazonaws.com/myinterviewtrainer-domestic/public_assets/assets/000/000/329/original/sorting_of_values_in_array.png?1618934847\" class=\"lazy-elem\"\u003E\u003C/figure\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"why-does-the-java-array-index-start-with-0\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E36. Why does the java array index start with 0?\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cp\u003EIt is because the 0 index array avoids the extra arithmetic operation to calculate the memory address.\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cp\u003EExample - Consider the array and assume each element takes 4-byte memory space. Then the address will be like this -\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cfigure class=\"image image_resized\" style=\"width:75%;\"\u003E\u003Cimg data-src=\"https://d3n0h9tb65y8q.cloudfront.net/public_assets/assets/000/003/024/original/4-byte_memory_space.png?1648814139\" class=\"lazy-elem\"\u003E\u003C/figure\u003E\u003Cp\u003ENow if we want to access index 4. Then internally java calculates the address using the formula-\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003E[Base Address + (index * no_of_bytes)]\u003C/strong\u003E. So according to this. The starting address of the index 4 will be - \u003Cstrong\u003E[100 + (4*4)] = 116\u003C/strong\u003E. And exactly that's what the address is calculated. \u003Cbr\u003ENow consider the same with 1 index Array -\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cfigure class=\"image image_resized\" style=\"width:75%;\"\u003E\u003Cimg data-src=\"https://d3n0h9tb65y8q.cloudfront.net/public_assets/assets/000/003/025/original/4-byte_memory_space_with_1_index_array.png?1648814164\" class=\"lazy-elem\"\u003E\u003C/figure\u003E\u003Cp\u003ENow if we apply the same formula here. Then we get - \u003Cstrong\u003E116\u003C/strong\u003E as the starting address of the 4th index. Which is wrong. Then we need to apply formula - [\u003Cstrong\u003EBase Address + ((index-1) * no_of_bytes)]\u003C/strong\u003E.\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cp\u003EAnd for calculating this, an extra arithmetic operation has to be performed. And consider the case where millions of addresses need to be calculated, this causes complexity. So to avoid this, ) the index array is supported by java.\u003C/p\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"why-is-the-remove-method-faster-in-the-linked-list-than-in-an-array\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E37. Why is the remove method faster in the linked list than in an array?\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cp\u003EIn the linked list, we only need to adjust the references when we want to delete the element from either end or the front of the linked list. But in the array, indexes are used. So to manage proper indexing, we need to adjust the values from the array So this adjustment of value is costlier than the adjustment of references.\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EExample\u003C/strong\u003E - To Delete from the front of the linked list, internally the references adjustments happened like this.\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cfigure class=\"image image_resized\" style=\"width:75%;\"\u003E\u003Cimg data-src=\"https://d3n0h9tb65y8q.cloudfront.net/public_assets/assets/000/003/027/original/Delete_from_the_front_of_the_linked_list.png?1648814824\" class=\"lazy-elem\"\u003E\u003C/figure\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThe only thing that will change is that the head pointer will point to the heads next node. And delete the previous node. That is the constant time operation.\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cp\u003EWhereas in the ArrayList, internally it should work like this-\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cfigure class=\"image image_resized\" style=\"width:75%;\"\u003E\u003Cimg data-src=\"https://d3n0h9tb65y8q.cloudfront.net/public_assets/assets/000/003/028/original/ArrayList.png?1648814946\" class=\"lazy-elem\"\u003E\u003C/figure\u003E\u003Cp\u003EFor deletion of the first element, all the next element has to move to one place ahead. So this copying value takes time. So that is the reason why removing in ArrayList is slower than LinkedList.\u003C/p\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"how-many-overloaded-add-and-addall-methods-are-available-in-the-list-interface-describe-the-need-and-uses\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E38. How many overloaded add() and addAll() methods are available in the List interface? Describe the need and uses.\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cp\u003EThere are a total of 4 overloaded methods for add() and addAll() methods available in List Interface. The below table states the description of all.\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cfigure class=\"table\"\u003E\u003Ctable\u003E\n\u003Cthead\u003E\u003Ctr\u003E\n\u003Cth\u003EReturn Type\u003C/th\u003E\n\u003Cth\u003EMethod Description\u003C/th\u003E\n\u003C/tr\u003E\u003C/thead\u003E\n\u003Ctbody\u003E\n\u003Ctr\u003E\n\u003Cth\u003Eboolean\u003C/th\u003E\n\u003Ctd\u003E\n\u003Cstrong\u003Eadd(Element e)\u003C/strong\u003E: This method is used for adding the element at the end of the List. The Datatype of the element is of any type it has been initially assigned with. It returns the boolean indicating successfully inserted or not.\u003C/td\u003E\n\u003C/tr\u003E\n\u003Ctr\u003E\n\u003Cth\u003Evoid\u003C/th\u003E\n\u003Ctd\u003E\n\u003Cstrong\u003Eadd(int index, Element e)\u003C/strong\u003E: This method is the overloaded version of add() method. In this, along with the element, the index is also passed to the method for the specific index the value needs to be inserted. \u003C/td\u003E\n\u003C/tr\u003E\n\u003Ctr\u003E\n\u003Cth\u003Eboolean\u003C/th\u003E\n\u003Ctd\u003E\n\u003Cstrong\u003EaddAll(Collection <extends ? Element > c)\u003C/strong\u003E: This method helps to add all elements at the end of collections from the list received in the parameter. It contains an iterator that helps to iterate the list and add the elements to the collection.\u003C/td\u003E\n\u003C/tr\u003E\n\u003Ctr\u003E\n\u003Cth\u003Eboolean\u003C/th\u003E\n\u003Ctd\u003E\n\u003Cstrong\u003EaddAll(int index, Collection <extends ? Element > c)\u003C/strong\u003E: This is the overloaded method for addAll() method. In this along with the list, we can pass the specified index from which the list elements need to be added.\u003C/td\u003E\n\u003C/tr\u003E\n\u003C/tbody\u003E\n\u003C/table\u003E\u003C/figure\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"how-does-the-size-of-arraylist-grow-dynamically-and-also-state-how-it-is-implemented-internally\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E39. How does the size of ArrayList grow dynamically? And also state how it is implemented internally.\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cp\u003EArrayList is implemented in such a way that it can grow dynamically. We don't need to specify the size of ArrayList. For adding the values in it, the methodology it uses is -\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cp\u003E1. Consider initially that there are 2 elements in the ArrayList. \u003Cstrong\u003E[2, 3]\u003C/strong\u003E.\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cfigure class=\"image image_resized\" style=\"width:50%;\"\u003E\u003Cimg data-src=\"https://d3n0h9tb65y8q.cloudfront.net/public_assets/assets/000/003/030/original/step_1.png?1648815057\" class=\"lazy-elem\"\u003E\u003C/figure\u003E\u003Cp\u003E2. If we need to add the element into this. Then internally what will happen is-\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cul\u003E\u003Cli\u003EArrayList will allocate the new ArrayList of Size (current size + half of the current size). And add the old elements into the new. Old - [2, 3], New - [2, 3, null].\u003C/li\u003E\u003C/ul\u003E\u003Cfigure class=\"image image_resized\" style=\"width:50%;\"\u003E\u003Cimg data-src=\"https://d3n0h9tb65y8q.cloudfront.net/public_assets/assets/000/003/817/original/ArrayList.png?1677134979\" class=\"lazy-elem\"\u003E\u003C/figure\u003E\u003Cul\u003E\u003Cli\u003EThen the new value will be inserted into it. [2, 3, 4, null]. And for the next time, the extra space will be available for the value to be inserted.\u003C/li\u003E\u003C/ul\u003E\u003Cfigure class=\"image image_resized\" style=\"width:50%;\"\u003E\u003Cimg data-src=\"https://d3n0h9tb65y8q.cloudfront.net/public_assets/assets/000/003/031/original/step_2_b.png?1648815222\" class=\"lazy-elem\"\u003E\u003C/figure\u003E\u003Cp\u003E3. This process continues and the time taken to perform all of these is considered as the amortized constant time. \u003C/p\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThis is how the ArrayList grows dynamically. And when we delete any entry from the ArrayList then the following steps are performed -\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cp\u003E1. It searches for the element index in the array. Searching takes some time. Typically its O(n) because it needs to search for the element in the entire array.\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cfigure class=\"image image_resized\" style=\"width:50%;\"\u003E\u003Cimg data-src=\"https://d3n0h9tb65y8q.cloudfront.net/public_assets/assets/000/003/034/original/step_3-a.png?1648815295\" class=\"lazy-elem\"\u003E\u003C/figure\u003E\u003Cp\u003E2. After searching the element, it needs to shift the element from the right side to fill the index.\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cfigure class=\"image image_resized\" style=\"width:50%;\"\u003E\u003Cimg data-src=\"https://d3n0h9tb65y8q.cloudfront.net/public_assets/assets/000/003/035/original/Step_3-b.png?1648815333\" class=\"lazy-elem\"\u003E\u003C/figure\u003E\u003Cp\u003ESo this is how the elements are deleted from the ArrayList internally. Similarly, the search operations are also implemented internally as defined in removing elements from the list (searching for elements to delete).\u003C/p\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n\n \u003C/div\u003E\n \u003Cdiv\n data-scroll-id=\"2\"\n data-scroll-identifier=\"each-article-section\"\n id=\"experienced\"\n \u003E\n \u003Ch2\u003EJava Interview Questions for Experienced\u003C/h2\u003E\n\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"although-inheritance-is-a-popular-oop-concept-it-is-less-advantageous-than-composition-explain\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E1. Although inheritance is a popular OOPs concept, it is less advantageous than composition. Explain.\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cp\u003EInheritance lags behind composition in the following scenarios:\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cul\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EMultiple-inheritance is not possible in Java. Classes can only extend from one superclass. In cases where multiple functionalities are required, for example - to read and write information into the file, the pattern of composition is preferred. The writer, as well as reader functionalities, can be made use of by considering them as the private members.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EComposition assists in attaining high flexibility and prevents breaking of encapsulation.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EUnit testing is possible with composition and not inheritance. When a developer wants to test a class composing a different class, then Mock Object can be created for signifying the composed class to facilitate testing. This technique is not possible with the help of inheritance as the derived class cannot be tested without the help of the superclass in inheritance.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EThe loosely coupled nature of composition is preferable over the tightly coupled nature of inheritance.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003C/ul\u003E\u003Cp\u003ELets take an example:\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cpre\u003E\u003Ccode class=\"language-java hljs\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Epackage\u003C/span\u003E comparison;\n\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Epublic\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-class\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eclass\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-title\"\u003ETop\u003C/span\u003E \u003C/span\u003E{\n\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-function\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Epublic\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eint\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-title\"\u003Estart\u003C/span\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-params\"\u003E()\u003C/span\u003E \u003C/span\u003E{\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Ereturn\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-number\"\u003E0\u003C/span\u003E;\n}\n}\n\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-class\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eclass\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-title\"\u003EBottom\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eextends\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-title\"\u003ETop\u003C/span\u003E \u003C/span\u003E{\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-function\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Epublic\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eint\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-title\"\u003Estop\u003C/span\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-params\"\u003E()\u003C/span\u003E \u003C/span\u003E{\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Ereturn\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-number\"\u003E0\u003C/span\u003E;\n }\n}\u003C/code\u003E\u003C/pre\u003E\u003Cp\u003EIn the above example, inheritance is followed. Now, some modifications are done to the Top class like this:\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cpre\u003E\u003Ccode class=\"language-java hljs\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Epublic\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-class\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eclass\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-title\"\u003ETop\u003C/span\u003E \u003C/span\u003E{\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-function\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Epublic\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eint\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-title\"\u003Estart\u003C/span\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-params\"\u003E()\u003C/span\u003E \u003C/span\u003E{\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Ereturn\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-number\"\u003E0\u003C/span\u003E;\n }\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-function\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Epublic\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Evoid\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-title\"\u003Estop\u003C/span\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-params\"\u003E()\u003C/span\u003E \u003C/span\u003E{\n }\n}\u003C/code\u003E\u003C/pre\u003E\u003Cp\u003EIf the new implementation of the Top class is followed, a compile-time error is bound to occur in the Bottom class. Incompatible return type is there for the Top.stop() function. Changes have to be made to either the Top or the Bottom class to ensure compatibility. However, the composition technique can be utilized to solve the given problem:\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cpre\u003E\u003Ccode class=\"language-java hljs\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-class\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eclass\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-title\"\u003EBottom\u003C/span\u003E \u003C/span\u003E{\n Top par = \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Enew\u003C/span\u003E Top();\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-function\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Epublic\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eint\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-title\"\u003Estop\u003C/span\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-params\"\u003E()\u003C/span\u003E \u003C/span\u003E{\n par.start();\n par.stop();\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Ereturn\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-number\"\u003E0\u003C/span\u003E;\n }\n} \u003C/code\u003E\u003C/pre\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"difference-between-and-operators-in-java\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E2. What is the difference between >> and >>> operators in java?\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cp\u003EThese 2 are the bitwise right shift operators. Although both operators look similar. But there is a minimal difference between these two right shift operators.\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cul\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cstrong\u003E>> Bitwise Right Shift Operator\u003C/strong\u003E- This operator shifts each bit to its right position. And this maintains the signed bit.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cstrong\u003E>>> Bitwise Right Shift Operator with trailing zero\u003C/strong\u003E- This operator also shifts each bit to its right. But this doesnt maintain the signed bit. This operator makes the Most significant bit to 0.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003C/ul\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EExample-\u003C/strong\u003E Num1 = 8, Num2 = -8.\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cp\u003ESo the binary form of these numbers are - \u003C/p\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003ENum1 = 00000000 00000000 00000000 00001000 \u003C/strong\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003ENum2 = 11111111 11111111 11111111 11111000\u003C/strong\u003E\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003E>> Operator\u003C/strong\u003E : 8 >> 1 (Shift by one bit) : \u003C/p\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003ENum1 = 00000000 00000000 00000000 00000100\u003C/strong\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003ENum2 = 11111111 11111111 11111111 11111100\u003C/strong\u003E\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003E>>> Operator \u003C/strong\u003E: 8 >>> 1 (Shift by one bit) = \u003C/p\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003ENum1 = 00000000 00000000 00000000 00000100\u003C/strong\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003ENum2 = 01111111 11111111 11111111 11111100\u003C/strong\u003E\u003C/p\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"composition-vs-aggregation\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E3. What are Composition and Aggregation? State the difference.\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cp\u003EComposition, and Aggregation help to build (Has - A - Relationship) between classes and objects. But both are not the same in the end. \u003Cstrong\u003ELets understand with the help of an example. \u003C/strong\u003E\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cul\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EConsider the University as a class that has some departments in it. So the university will be the container object. And departments in it will contain objects. Now in this case, if the container object destroys then the contained objects will also get destroyed automatically. So here we can say that there is a strong association between the objects. So this Strong Association is called \u003Cstrong\u003EComposition\u003C/strong\u003E.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003ENow consider one more example. Suppose we have a class department and there are several professors' objects there in the department. Now if the department class is destroyed then the professor's object will become free to bind with other objects. Because container objects (Department) only hold the references of contained objects (Professors). So here is the weak association between the objects. And this weak association is called \u003Cstrong\u003EAggregation\u003C/strong\u003E.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003C/ul\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"string-literal-vs-new-string-object-in-java\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E4. How is the creation of a String using new() different from that of a literal?\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cp\u003EWhen a String is formed as a literal with the assistance of an assignment operator, it makes its way into the String constant pool so that String Interning can take place. This same object in the heap will be referenced by a different String if the content is the same for both of them.\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cpre\u003E\u003Ccode class=\"language-java hljs\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-function\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Epublic\u003C/span\u003E bool \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-title\"\u003Echecking\u003C/span\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-params\"\u003E()\u003C/span\u003E \u003C/span\u003E{\nString first = \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003E\"InterviewBit\"\u003C/span\u003E;\nString second = \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003E\"InterviewBit\"\u003C/span\u003E;\n\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eif\u003C/span\u003E (first == second)\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Ereturn\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Etrue\u003C/span\u003E;\n\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eelse\u003C/span\u003E\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Ereturn\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Efalse\u003C/span\u003E;\n}\u003C/code\u003E\u003C/pre\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThe checking() function will return true as the same content is referenced by both the variables.\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cfigure class=\"image image_resized\" style=\"width:75%;\"\u003E\u003Cimg data-src=\"https://s3.ap-south-1.amazonaws.com/myinterviewtrainer-domestic/public_assets/assets/000/000/337/original/string_pool_by_assignment_operator.png?1619005601\" class=\"lazy-elem\"\u003E\u003C/figure\u003E\u003Cp\u003EConversely, when a String formation takes place with the help of a new() operator, interning does not take place. The object gets created in the heap memory even if the same content object is present.\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cpre\u003E\u003Ccode class=\"language-java hljs\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-function\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Epublic\u003C/span\u003E bool \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-title\"\u003Echecking\u003C/span\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-params\"\u003E()\u003C/span\u003E \u003C/span\u003E{\nString first = \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Enew\u003C/span\u003E String(\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003E\"InterviewBit\"\u003C/span\u003E);\nString second = \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Enew\u003C/span\u003E String(\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003E\"InterviewBit\"\u003C/span\u003E);\n\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eif\u003C/span\u003E (first == second)\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Ereturn\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Etrue\u003C/span\u003E;\n\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eelse\u003C/span\u003E\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Ereturn\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Efalse\u003C/span\u003E;\n}\u003C/code\u003E\u003C/pre\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThe checking() function will return false as the same content is not referenced by both the variables.\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cfigure class=\"image image_resized\" style=\"width:75%;\"\u003E\u003Cimg data-src=\"https://s3.ap-south-1.amazonaws.com/myinterviewtrainer-domestic/public_assets/assets/000/000/338/original/string_pool_by_means_of_assignment_operator.png?1619005725\" class=\"lazy-elem\"\u003E\u003C/figure\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"how-is-the-new-operator-different-from-the-newinstance-operator-in-java\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E5. How is the new operator different from the newInstance() operator in java?\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cp\u003EBoth \u003Cstrong\u003Enew\u003C/strong\u003E and \u003Cstrong\u003EnewInstance()\u003C/strong\u003E operators are used to creating objects. The difference is- that when we already know the class name for which we have to create the object then we use a new operator. But suppose we dont know the class name for which we need to create the object, Or we get the class name from the command line argument, or the database, or the file. Then in that case we use the \u003Cstrong\u003EnewInstance()\u003C/strong\u003E operator.\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThe \u003Cstrong\u003EnewInstance()\u003C/strong\u003E keyword throws an exception that we need to handle. It is because there are chances that the class definition doesnt exist, and we get the class name from runtime. So it will throw an exception.\u003C/p\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"possible-to-increase-the-memory-limit-despite-having-garbage-collector-in-java-program\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E6. Is exceeding the memory limit possible in a program despite having a garbage collector?\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cp\u003EYes, it is possible for the program to go out of memory in spite of the presence of a garbage collector. Garbage collection assists in recognizing and eliminating those objects which are not required in the program anymore, in order to free up the resources used by them.\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cp\u003EIn a program, if an object is unreachable, then the execution of garbage collection takes place with respect to that object. If the amount of memory required for creating a new object is not sufficient, then memory is released for those objects which are no longer in the scope with the help of a garbage collector. The memory limit is exceeded for the program when the memory released is not enough for creating new objects.\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cp\u003EMoreover, exhaustion of the heap memory takes place if objects are created in such a manner that they remain in the scope and consume memory. The developer should make sure to dereference the object after its work is accomplished. Although the garbage collector endeavors its level best to reclaim memory as much as possible, memory limits can still be exceeded.\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cp\u003ELets take a look at the following example:\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cpre\u003E\u003Ccode class=\"language-java hljs\"\u003EList<String> example = \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Enew\u003C/span\u003E LinkedList<String>();\n\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Ewhile\u003C/span\u003E(\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Etrue\u003C/span\u003E){\nexample.add(\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Enew\u003C/span\u003E String(\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003E\"Memory Limit Exceeded\"\u003C/span\u003E));\n}\u003C/code\u003E\u003C/pre\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"explain-why-synchronization-is-important-in-java\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E7. Why is synchronization necessary? Explain with the help of a relevant example.\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cp\u003EConcurrent execution of different processes is made possible by synchronization. When a particular resource is shared between many threads, situations may arise in which multiple threads require the same shared resource.\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cp\u003ESynchronization assists in resolving the issue and the resource is shared by a single thread at a time. Lets take an example to understand it more clearly. For example, you have a URL and you have to find out the number of requests made to it. Two simultaneous requests can make the count erratic.\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003ENo synchronization:\u003C/strong\u003E\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cpre\u003E\u003Ccode class=\"language-java hljs\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Epackage\u003C/span\u003E anonymous;\n\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Epublic\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-class\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eclass\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-title\"\u003ECounting\u003C/span\u003E \u003C/span\u003E{\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eprivate\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eint\u003C/span\u003E increase_counter;\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-function\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Epublic\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eint\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-title\"\u003Eincrease\u003C/span\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-params\"\u003E()\u003C/span\u003E \u003C/span\u003E{\n increase_counter = increase_counter + \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-number\"\u003E1\u003C/span\u003E;\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Ereturn\u003C/span\u003E increase_counter;\n }\n}\u003C/code\u003E\u003C/pre\u003E\u003Cfigure class=\"image image_resized\" style=\"width:75%;\"\u003E\u003Cimg data-src=\"https://s3.ap-south-1.amazonaws.com/myinterviewtrainer-domestic/public_assets/assets/000/000/340/original/without_synchronization.png?1619006539\" class=\"lazy-elem\"\u003E\u003C/figure\u003E\u003Cp\u003EIf a thread Thread1 views the count as 10, it will be increased by 1 to 11. Simultaneously, if another thread Thread2 views the count as 10, it will be increased by 1 to 11. Thus, inconsistency in count values takes place because the expected final value is 12 but the actual final value we get will be 11.\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cp\u003ENow, the function increase() is made synchronized so that simultaneous accessing cannot take place.\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EWith synchronization:\u003C/strong\u003E\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cpre\u003E\u003Ccode class=\"language-java hljs\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Epackage\u003C/span\u003E anonymous;\n\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Epublic\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-class\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eclass\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-title\"\u003ECounting\u003C/span\u003E \u003C/span\u003E{\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eprivate\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eint\u003C/span\u003E increase_counter;\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-function\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Epublic\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Esynchronized\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eint\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-title\"\u003Eincrease\u003C/span\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-params\"\u003E()\u003C/span\u003E \u003C/span\u003E{\n increase_counter = increase_counter + \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-number\"\u003E1\u003C/span\u003E;\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Ereturn\u003C/span\u003E increase_counter;\n }\n}\u003C/code\u003E\u003C/pre\u003E\u003Cfigure class=\"image image_resized\" style=\"width:75%;\"\u003E\u003Cimg data-src=\"https://s3.ap-south-1.amazonaws.com/myinterviewtrainer-domestic/public_assets/assets/000/000/341/original/with_synchronization.png?1619006639\" class=\"lazy-elem\"\u003E\u003C/figure\u003E\u003Cp\u003EIf a thread Thread1 views the count as 10, it will be increased by 1 to 11, then the thread Thread2 will view the count as 11, it will be increased by 1 to 12. Thus, consistency in count values takes place.\u003C/p\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"what-is-the-significance-of-below-code-in-java\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E8. Define System.out.println().\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003ESystem.out.println()\u003C/strong\u003E is used to print the message on the console. \u003Cstrong\u003ESystem\u003C/strong\u003E - It is a class present in \u003Cstrong\u003Ejava.lang package\u003C/strong\u003E. Out is the static variable of type PrintStream class present in the \u003Cstrong\u003ESystem class. println()\u003C/strong\u003E is the method present in the PrintStream class.\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cp\u003ESo if we justify the statement, then we can say that if we want to print anything on the console then we need to call the \u003Cstrong\u003Eprintln()\u003C/strong\u003E method that was present in PrintStream class. And we can call this using the output object that is present in the System class.\u003C/p\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"explain-java-thread-lifecycle\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E11. Can you explain the Java thread lifecycle?\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cp\u003EJava thread life cycle is as follows:\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cul\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cstrong\u003ENew\u003C/strong\u003E When the instance of the thread is created and the start() method has not been invoked, the thread is considered to be alive and hence in the NEW state.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cstrong\u003ERunnable\u003C/strong\u003E Once the start() method is invoked, before the run() method is called by JVM, the thread is said to be in RUNNABLE (ready to run) state. This state can also be entered from the Waiting or Sleeping state of the thread.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cstrong\u003ERunning\u003C/strong\u003E When the run() method has been invoked and the thread starts its execution, the thread is said to be in a RUNNING state.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cstrong\u003ENon-Runnable (Blocked/Waiting)\u003C/strong\u003E When the thread is not able to run despite the fact of its aliveness, the thread is said to be in a NON-RUNNABLE state. Ideally, after some time of its aliveness, the thread should go to a runnable state.\u003Cul\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EA thread is said to be in a Blocked state if it wants to enter synchronized code but it is unable to as another thread is operating in that synchronized block on the same object. The first thread has to wait until the other thread exits the synchronized block.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EA thread is said to be in a Waiting state if it is waiting for the signal to execute from another thread, i.e it waits for work until the signal is received.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003C/ul\u003E\n\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cstrong\u003ETerminated\u003C/strong\u003E Once the run() method execution is completed, the thread is said to enter the TERMINATED step and is considered to not be alive.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003C/ul\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThe following flowchart clearly explains the lifecycle of the thread in Java.\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cfigure class=\"image\"\u003E\u003Cimg data-src=\"https://s3.ap-south-1.amazonaws.com/myinterviewtrainer-domestic/public_assets/assets/000/000/347/original/java_thread_lifecycle.jpg?1619072391\" class=\"lazy-elem\"\u003E\u003C/figure\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"reason-for-tradeoff-between-usage-of-unordered-array-vs-usage-of-ordered-array\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E12. What could be the tradeoff between the usage of an unordered array versus the usage of an ordered array?\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cul\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EThe main advantage of having an ordered array is the reduced search time complexity of \u003Ccode\u003EO(log n)\u003C/code\u003E whereas the time complexity in an unordered array is \u003Ccode\u003EO(n)\u003C/code\u003E.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EThe main drawback of the ordered array is its increased insertion time which is O(n) due to the fact that its element has to reordered to maintain the order of array during every insertion whereas the time complexity in the unordered array is only O(1).\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EConsidering the above 2 key points and depending on what kind of scenario a developer requires, the appropriate data structure can be used for implementation.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003C/ul\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"can-we-import-same-class-or-package-twice-in-java-and-what-happens-during-runtime\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E13. Is it possible to import the same class or package twice in Java and what happens to it during runtime?\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cp\u003EIt is possible to import a class or package more than once, however, it is redundant because the JVM internally loads the package or class only once.\u003C/p\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"if-a-package-has-subpackages-will-it-suffice-to-import-only-the-main-package\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E14. In case a package has sub packages, will it suffice to import only the main package? e.g. Does importing of com.myMainPackage.* also import com.myMainPackage.mySubPackage.*?\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cp\u003EThis is a big NO. We need to understand that the importing of the sub-packages of a package needs to be done explicitly. Importing the parent package only results in the import of the classes within it and not the contents of its child/sub-packages.\u003C/p\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"will-finally-block-be-executed-if-code-system-exit-0-is-written-at-the-end-of-try-block\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E15. Will the finally block be executed if the code System.exit(0) is written at the end of try block?\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cp\u003ENO. The control of the program post \u003Ccode\u003ESystem.exit(0)\u003C/code\u003E is immediately gone and the program gets terminated which is why the finally block never gets executed.\u003C/p\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"java-marker-interfaces\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E16. What do you understand by marker interfaces in Java?\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cp\u003EMarker interfaces, also known as tagging interfaces are those interfaces that have no methods and constants defined in them. They are there for helping the compiler and JVM to get run time-related information regarding the objects.\u003C/p\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"explain-double-brace-initialization-in-java\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E17. Explain the term Double Brace Initialisation in Java?\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cp\u003EThis is a convenient means of initializing any collections in Java. Consider the below example.\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cpre\u003E\u003Ccode class=\"language-java hljs\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eimport\u003C/span\u003E java.util.HashSet;\n\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eimport\u003C/span\u003E java.util.Set;\n \n\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Epublic\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-class\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eclass\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-title\"\u003EIBDoubleBraceDemo\u003C/span\u003E\u003C/span\u003E{\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-function\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Epublic\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Estatic\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Evoid\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-title\"\u003Emain\u003C/span\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-params\"\u003E(String[] args)\u003C/span\u003E\u003C/span\u003E{\n Set<String> stringSets = \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Enew\u003C/span\u003E HashSet<String>()\n {\n {\n add(\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003E\"set1\"\u003C/span\u003E);\n add(\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003E\"set2\"\u003C/span\u003E);\n add(\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003E\"set3\"\u003C/span\u003E);\n }\n };\n \n doSomething(stringSets);\n }\n \n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-function\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eprivate\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Estatic\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan stringSets)\u003C/span\u003E\u003C/span\u003E{\n System.out.println(stringSets);\n }\n}\u003C/code\u003E\u003C/pre\u003E\u003Cp\u003EIn the above example, we see that the stringSets were initialized by using double braces.\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cul\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EThe first brace does the task of creating an anonymous inner class that has the capability of accessing the parent classs behavior. In our example, we are creating the subclass of HashSet so that it can use the add() method of HashSet.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EThe second braces do the task of initializing the instances.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003C/ul\u003E\u003Cp\u003ECare should be taken while initializing through this method as the method involves the creation of anonymous inner classes which can cause problems during the garbage collection or serialization processes and may also result in memory leaks.\u003C/p\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"why-is-string-length-not-accurate\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E18. Why is it said that the length() method of String class doesn't return accurate results?\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cul\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EThe length method returns the number of Unicode units of the String. Let's understand what Unicode units are and what is the confusion below.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EWe know that Java uses UTF-16 for String representation. With this Unicode, we need to understand the below two Unicode related terms:\u003Cul\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003ECode Point: This represents an integer denoting a character in the code space.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003ECode Unit: This is a bit sequence used for encoding the code points. In order to do this, one or more units might be required for representing a code point.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003C/ul\u003E\n\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EUnder the UTF-16 scheme, the code points were divided logically into 17 planes and the first plane was called the Basic Multilingual Plane (BMP). The BMP has classic characters - U+0000 to U+FFFF. The rest of the characters- U+10000 to U+10FFFF were termed as the supplementary characters as they were contained in the remaining planes.\u003Cul\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EThe code points from the first plane are encoded using \u003Cstrong\u003Eone\u003C/strong\u003E 16-bit code unit\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EThe code points from the remaining planes are encoded using \u003Cstrong\u003Etwo\u003C/strong\u003E code units.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003C/ul\u003E\n\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003C/ul\u003E\u003Cp\u003ENow if a string contained supplementary characters, the length function would count that as 2 units and the result of the length() function would not be as per what is expected.\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cp\u003EIn other words, if there is 1 supplementary character of 2 units, the length of that SINGLE character is considered to be TWO - Notice the inaccuracy here? As per the java documentation, it is expected, but as per the real logic, it is inaccurate.\u003C/p\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"explain-output-of-below-java-code\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E19. What is the output of the below code and why?\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cpre\u003E\u003Ccode class=\"language-java hljs\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Epublic\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-class\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eclass\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-title\"\u003EInterviewBit\u003C/span\u003E\u003C/span\u003E{\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-function\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Epublic\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Estatic\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Evoid\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-title\"\u003Emain\u003C/span\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-params\"\u003E(String[] args)\u003C/span\u003E\n \u003C/span\u003E{\n System.out.println(\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003E'b'\u003C/span\u003E + \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003E'i'\u003C/span\u003E + \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003E't'\u003C/span\u003E);\n }\n}\u003C/code\u003E\u003C/pre\u003E\u003Cp\u003Ebit would have been the result printed if the letters were used in double-quotes (or the string literals). But the question has the character literals (single quotes) being used which is why concatenation wouldn't occur. The corresponding ASCII values of each character would be added and the result of that sum would be printed.\u003Cbr\u003EThe ASCII values of b, i, t are:\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cul\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003Eb = 98\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003Ei = 105\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003Et = 116\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003C/ul\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ccode\u003E98 + 105 + 116 = 319\u003C/code\u003E\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cp\u003EHence 319 would be printed.\u003C/p\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"how-can-we-make-objects-eligible-for-garbage-collection-in-java\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E20. What are the possible ways of making object eligible for garbage collection (GC) in Java?\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EFirst Approach:\u003C/strong\u003E Set the object references to null once the object creation purpose is served.\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cpre\u003E\u003Ccode class=\"language-java hljs\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Epublic\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-class\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eclass\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-title\"\u003EIBGarbageCollect\u003C/span\u003E \u003C/span\u003E{\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-function\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Epublic\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Estatic\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Evoid\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-title\"\u003Emain\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-params\"\u003E(String [] args)\u003C/span\u003E\u003C/span\u003E{\n String s1 = \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003E\"Some String\"\u003C/span\u003E;\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-comment\"\u003E// s1 referencing String object - not yet eligible for GC\u003C/span\u003E\n s1 = \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Enull\u003C/span\u003E; \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-comment\"\u003E// now s1 is eligible for GC\u003C/span\u003E\n }\n }\u003C/code\u003E\u003C/pre\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003ESecond Approach:\u003C/strong\u003E Point the reference variable to another object. Doing this, the object which the reference variable was referencing before becomes eligible for GC.\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cpre\u003E\u003Ccode class=\"language-java hljs\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Epublic\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-class\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eclass\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-title\"\u003EIBGarbageCollect\u003C/span\u003E \u003C/span\u003E{\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-function\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Epublic\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Estatic\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Evoid\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-title\"\u003Emain\u003C/span\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-params\"\u003E(String [] args)\u003C/span\u003E\u003C/span\u003E{\n String s1 = \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003E\"To Garbage Collect\"\u003C/span\u003E;\n String s2 = \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003E\"Another Object\"\u003C/span\u003E;\n System.out.println(s1); \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-comment\"\u003E// s1 is not yet eligible for GC\u003C/span\u003E\n s1 = s2; \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-comment\"\u003E// Point s1 to other object pointed by s2\u003C/span\u003E\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-comment\"\u003E/* Here, the string object having the content \"To Garbage Collect\" is not referred by any reference variable. Therefore, it is eligible for GC */\u003C/span\u003E\n }\n}\u003C/code\u003E\u003C/pre\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EThird Approach: \u003C/strong\u003EIsland of Isolation Approach: When 2 reference variables pointing to instances of the same class, and these variables refer to only each other and the objects pointed by these 2 variables don't have any other references, then it is said to have formed an Island of Isolation and these 2 objects are eligible for GC.\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cpre\u003E\u003Ccode class=\"language-java hljs\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Epublic\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-class\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eclass\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-title\"\u003EIBGarbageCollect\u003C/span\u003E \u003C/span\u003E{\n IBGarbageCollect ib; \n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-function\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Epublic\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Estatic\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Evoid\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-title\"\u003Emain\u003C/span\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-params\"\u003E(String [] str)\u003C/span\u003E\u003C/span\u003E{\n IBGarbageCollect ibgc1 = \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Enew\u003C/span\u003E IBGarbageCollect();\n IBGarbageCollect ibgc2 = \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Enew\u003C/span\u003E IBGarbageCollect();\n ibgc1.ib = ibgc2; \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-comment\"\u003E//ibgc1 points to ibgc2\u003C/span\u003E\n ibgc2.ib = ibgc1; \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-comment\"\u003E//ibgc2 points to ibgc1\u003C/span\u003E\n ibgc1 = \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Enull\u003C/span\u003E;\n ibgc2 = \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Enull\u003C/span\u003E;\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-comment\"\u003E/* \n * We see that ibgc1 and ibgc2 objects refer \n * to only each other and have no valid \n * references- these 2 objects for island of isolcation - eligible for GC\n */\u003C/span\u003E\n }\n}\u003C/code\u003E\u003C/pre\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"how-many-objects-are-eligible-for-garbage-collection\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E21. Lets visually understand what's happening in the code.\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cfigure class=\"image image_resized\" style=\"width:75%;\"\u003E\u003Cimg data-src=\"https://d3n0h9tb65y8q.cloudfront.net/public_assets/assets/000/003/029/original/7_objects_will_be_eligible_for_garbage_collection.png?1648815020\" class=\"lazy-elem\"\u003E\u003C/figure\u003E\u003Cfigure class=\"image image_resized\" style=\"width:75%;\"\u003E\u003Cimg data-src=\"https://d3n0h9tb65y8q.cloudfront.net/public_assets/assets/000/003/037/original/step4.png?1648815510\" class=\"lazy-elem\"\u003E\u003C/figure\u003E\u003Cp\u003EIn the above figure on line 3, we can see that on each array index we are declaring a new array so the reference will be of that new array on all the 3 indexes. So the old array will be pointed to by none. So these three are eligible for garbage collection. And on line 4, we are creating a new array object on the older reference. So that will point to a new array and older multidimensional objects will become eligible for garbage collection.\u003C/p\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"what-is-the-best-way-to-inject-dependency-also-state-the-reason\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E22. What is the best way to inject dependency? Also, state the reason.\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cp\u003EThere is no boundation for using a particular dependency injection. But the recommended approach is - \u003C/p\u003E\u003Cp\u003ESetters are mostly recommended for optional dependencies injection, and constructor arguments are recommended for mandatory ones. This is because constructor injection enables the injection of values into immutable fields and enables reading them more easily.\u003C/p\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"how-we-can-set-the-spring-bean-scope-and-what-supported-scopes-does-it-have\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E23. How we can set the spring bean scope. And what supported scopes does it have?\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cp\u003EA scope can be set by an annotation such as the @Scope annotation or the \"scope\" attribute in an XML configuration file. Spring Bean supports the following five scopes:\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cul\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003ESingleton\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EPrototype\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003ERequest\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003ESession\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EGlobal-session\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003C/ul\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"what-are-the-different-categories-of-java-design-patterns\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E24. What are the different categories of Java Design patterns?\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cp\u003EJava Design patterns are categorized into the following different types. And those are also further categorized as \u003C/p\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EStructural patterns:\u003C/strong\u003E\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cul\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EAdapter\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EBridge\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EFilter\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EComposite\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EDecorator\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EFacade\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EFlyweight\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EProxy\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003C/ul\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EBehavioral patterns:\u003C/strong\u003E\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cul\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EInterpreter\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003ETemplate method/ pattern\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EChain of responsibility\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003ECommand pattern\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EIterator pattern\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EStrategy pattern\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EVisitor pattern\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003C/ul\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EJ2EE patterns:\u003C/strong\u003E\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cul\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EMVC Pattern\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EData Access Object pattern\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EFront controller pattern\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EIntercepting filter pattern\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003ETransfer object pattern\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003C/ul\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003ECreational patterns:\u003C/strong\u003E\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cul\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EFactory method/Template\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EAbstract Factory\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EBuilder\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EPrototype\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003ESingleton\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003C/ul\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"what-is-a-memory-leak-discuss-some-common-causes-of-it\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E25. What is a Memory Leak? Discuss some common causes of it.\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cp\u003EThe Java Garbage Collector (GC) typically removes unused objects when they are no longer required, but when they are still referenced, the unused objects cannot be removed. So this causes the memory leak problem. \u003Cstrong\u003EExample \u003C/strong\u003E- Consider a linked list like the structure below -\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cfigure class=\"image image_resized\" style=\"width:75%;\"\u003E\u003Cimg data-src=\"https://d3n0h9tb65y8q.cloudfront.net/public_assets/assets/000/003/036/original/Memory_Leak_Discuss_some_common_causes_of_it.png?1648815404\" class=\"lazy-elem\"\u003E\u003C/figure\u003E\u003Cp\u003EIn the above image, there are unused objects that are not referenced. But then also Garbage collection will not free it. Because it is referencing some existing referenced object. So this can be the situation of memory leak.\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003ESome common causes of Memory leaks are\u003C/strong\u003E - \u003C/p\u003E\u003Cul\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EWhen there are Unbounded caches.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EExcessive page swapping is done by the operating system.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EImproper written custom data structures.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EInserting into a collection object without first deleting it.\u003Cbr\u003Eetc.\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003C/ul\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"assume-a-thread-has-a-lock-on-it-calling-the-sleep-method-on-that-thread-will-release-the-lock\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E26. Write a Java Program to check if any number is a magic number or not. A number is said to be a magic number if after doing sum of digits in each step and inturn doing sum of digits of that sum, the ultimate result (when there is only one digit left) is 1.\u003C/h3\u003E\n \u003Carticle class=\"ibpage-article\"\u003E\n \u003Cp\u003EExample, consider the number:\u003C/p\u003E\u003Cul\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EStep 1: 163 => 1+6+3 = 10\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EStep 2: 10 => 1+0 = 1 => Hence 163 is a magic number\u003C/li\u003E\n\u003C/ul\u003E\u003Cpre\u003E\u003Ccode class=\"language-java hljs\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Epublic\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-class\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eclass\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-title\"\u003EIBMagicNumber\u003C/span\u003E\u003C/span\u003E{\n\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-function\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Epublic\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Estatic\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Evoid\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-title\"\u003Emain\u003C/span\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-params\"\u003E(String[] args)\u003C/span\u003E \u003C/span\u003E{ \n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eint\u003C/span\u003E num = \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-number\"\u003E163\u003C/span\u003E; Case.\u003C/span\u003E\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eif\u003C/span\u003E(low > high)\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Ereturn\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Efalse\u003C/span\u003E;\n \n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-comment\"\u003E//Checking if the key is found in the middle.\u003C/span\u003E\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eif\u003C/span\u003E(arr[mid] == key)\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Ereturn\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Etrue\u003C/span\u003E;\n \n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-comment\"\u003E//Searching on the left half if a key exists there. \u003C/span\u003E\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eif\u003C/span\u003E(key < arr[mid])\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Ereturn\u003C/span\u003E binarySearch(arr, low, mid-\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-number\"\u003E1\u003C/span\u003E, key);\n \n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-comment\"\u003E//Searching on the other half otherwise.\u003C/span\u003E\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Ereturn\u003C/span\u003E binarySearch(arr, mid+\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-number\"\u003E1\u003C/span\u003E, high, key);\n }\n\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-function\"\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Epublic\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Estatic\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Evoid\u003C/span\u003E \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-title\"\u003Emain\u003C/span\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-params\"\u003E(String[] args)\u003C/span\u003E \u003C/span\u003E{\n \n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eint\u003C/span\u003E[] arr = {\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-number\"\u003E2\u003C/span\u003E, \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-number\"\u003E5\u003C/span\u003E, \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-number\"\u003E9\u003C/span\u003E, \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-number\"\u003E13\u003C/span\u003E, \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-number\"\u003E17\u003C/span\u003E, \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-number\"\u003E21\u003C/span\u003E, \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-number\"\u003E30\u003C/span\u003E};\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eif\u003C/span\u003E(binarySearch(arr, \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-number\"\u003E0\u003C/span\u003E, (arr.length-\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-number\"\u003E1\u003C/span\u003E), \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-number\"\u003E30\u003C/span\u003E))\n System.out.println(\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003E\" Element Found. \"\u003C/span\u003E);\n \u003Cspan class=\"hljs-keyword\"\u003Eelse\u003C/span\u003E\n System.out.println(\u003Cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003E\" Element not Found.\"\u003C/span\u003E);\n}\n}\u003C/code\u003E\u003C/pre\u003E\u003Cp\u003EIn the above code, we are finding the middle element each time and checking if the element is in the middle or not. If it is not, then we check on which side from the middle it exists. And Recursively searching on the particular subarray. So this way we are reducing the search space by 2 every time. So the search time is very low.\u003C/p\u003E\n \u003C/article\u003E\n \u003C/section\u003E\n\n \u003C/div\u003E\n \u003Cdiv\n data-scroll-id=\"4\"\n data-scroll-identifier=\"each-article-section\"\n id=\"conclusion\"\n \u003E\n \u003Ch2\u003EConclusion\u003C/h2\u003E\n\n \u003Csection class=\"ibpage-article-header\" id=\"conclusion\"\u003E\n \u003Ch3\u003E1.
